ਅਸ਼ੀਰਵਾਦ

ਤਸੀਂ ਜੋ ਆਪਣੇ ਪਿਤਾ ਭਾਈ ਹੀਰਾ ਸਿੰਘ ਜੀ ਦੀ ਜੀਵਨੀ ਲਿਖਣ ਦਾ ਫ਼ੈਸਲਾ ਕੀਤਾ
ਹੋ ਉਹ ਬੜਾ ਸ਼ਲਾਘਾ ਯੋਗ ਹੈ। ਇਹ ਜੀਵਨੀ ਇੱਕ ਐਸੇ ਪੂਜਨੀਕ ਗੁਰਸਿੱਖ ਦੀ ਹੈ, ਜਿਹੜੀ
ਹਰ ਇੱਕ ਸਿੱਖ ਨੂੰ ਆਪਣੇ ਜੀਵਨ ਲਈ ਰੌਸ਼ਨੀ ਦੇਵੇਗੀ। ਐਸੇ ਨਿਰਸੋਲਕ ਸੇਵਕ, ਪੂਰਨ
ਗੁਰਸਿੱਖ, ਉੱਚ ਕੋਟੀ ਦੇ ਕੀਰਤਨੀਏ, ਲੋਭ-ਮੋਹ-ਹੰਕਾਰ ਤੋਂ ਰਹਿਤ ਕੋਈ ਵਿਰਲਾ ਹੀ ਲੱਭੇਗਾ।
ਵਾਹਿਗੁਰੂ ਅਜਿਹੇ ਸੱਜਣ ਆਪਣੀ ਕਿਰਪਾ ਦੁਆਰਾ ਕਦੀ-ਕਦਾਈਂ ਹੀ ਆਮ ਲੋਕਾਂ ਦੇ ਲਾਭ
ਲਈ ਭੇਜਦਾ ਹੈ ਜੋ ਕਿ ਆਪਣੀ ਛਾਪ ਛੱਡ ਜਾਂਦੇ ਹਨ, ਜਿਹੜੀ ਕਿ ਸਦਾ ਲਈ ਆਪਣਾ ਅਸਰ
ਦਰਸਾਉਂਦੀ ਰਹਿੰਦੀ ਹੈ।
ਤੁਸੀ ਜਿਤਨੀ ਮਿਹਨਤ ਕੀਤੀ ਹੈ ਤੇ ਇਰ ਸਾਰਾ ਮਸਾਲਾ ਇਕੱਠਾ ਕੀਤਾ ਹੈ, ਇਹ ਵੀ
ਤੁਹਾਡਾ ਪੰਥ 'ਤੇ ਅਹਿਸਾਨ ਹੈ। ਇਤਨਾ ਖ਼ਰਚ ਕਰਕੇ, ਐਨੇ ਦੌਰੇ ਕਰਕੇ ਵੱਖਰੀਆਂ-ਵੱਖਰੀਆਂ
ਥਾਵਾਂ ਤੋਂ ਇਹ ਸਭ ਕੁਝ ਇਕੱਠਾ ਕਰਨਾ, ਇਹ ਵੀ ਤੁਹਾਡੀ ਵੱਡੀ ਘਾਲਨਾ ਹੈਂ ਤੇ ਪੰਥ 'ਤੇ
ਤੁਹਾਡਾ ਪਰਉਪਕਾਰ ਹੈ। ਇਸ ਜੀਵਨੀ ਨੂੰ ਪੜ੍ਹ ਕੇ ਸਿੱਖ ਲਾਭ ਉਠਾਉਂਦੇ ਰਹਿਣਗੇ ਅਤੇ ਆਪਣੇ
ਆਚਰਨ ਬਤੌਰ ਇੱਕ ਗੁਰਸਿੱਖ ਦੇ ਗੁਜ਼ਾਰਨ ਲਈ ਇਹ ਆਪਣਾ ਚਾਨਣਾ ਦਿੰਦੀ ਰਹੇਗੀ। ਮੈਂ
ਆਪ ਨੂੰ ਮੁਬਾਰਕਬਾਦ ਦਿੰਦਾ ਹਾਂ।
6-ਏ ਰਿੰਗ ਰੋਡ, ਹੁਕਮ ਸਿੰਘ
ਨਵੀਂ ਦਿੱਲੀ ਰੀ ਸਾਬਕਾ ਸਪੀਕਰ ਲੋਕ ਸਭਾ,
15 ਸਤੰਬਰ 1980 ਸਾਬਕਾ ਗਵਰਨਰ ਰਾਜਸਥਾਨ
ਸੀ ਗੁਰੂ ਗ੍ਰੰਥ ਸਾਹਿਬ ਵਿੱਦਿਆ ਕੱਦਰ,

੧੫੬ ਕ੍ਰਾਰ੨ ` ਕੰ ਤੂੰ		 English (Meaning Translation)

**A Blessing**

Your decision to write the biography of your father, Bhai Hira Singh Ji, is highly commendable. This biography is about such a revered Gursikh who will provide light and guidance to every Sikh for their life.

It is rare to find such a selfless servant, a complete Gursikh, a Kirtan performer of the highest order, free from greed, attachment, and ego. Waheguru, through His grace, sends such noble souls only occasionally for the benefit of the common people, and they leave their indelible mark, which continues to show its effect forever.

The immense effort you have put in and the collection of all this material is also a great service to the Panth (the Sikh community). Spending so much, undertaking so many journeys, and gathering all this information from various places—this is a great endeavor and an act of benevolence towards the Panth.

By reading this biography, Sikhs will continue to benefit, and it will continue to provide guidance for them to lead their lives as Gursikhs. I congratulate you.

6-A Ring Road, Hukam Singh
New Delhi Former Speaker, Lok Sabha,
15 September 1980 Former Governor, Rajasthan
[UNCLEAR: Possible institution name followed by garbled text]

Notes
- Corrected likely OCR word: "ਨਿਰਸੋਲਕ" -> "ਨਿਰਸਵਾਰਥ" (reason: context requires 'selfless' or 'guileless' servant, fitting the list of virtues).
- Corrected likely OCR word: "ਇਰ" -> "ਇਹ" (reason: grammatical necessity, referring to 'this material').
- Unclear text: The final lines following "Former Governor, Rajasthan" are highly garbled OCR noise and have been marked as [UNCLEAR].

ਤਸੀਂ ਜੋ ਆਪਣੇ ਪਿਤਾ ਭਾਈ ਹੀਰਾ ਸਿੰਘ ਜੀ ਦੀ ਜੀਵਨੀ ਲਿਖਣ ਦਾ ਫ਼ੈਸਲਾ ਕੀਤਾ

ਗੁਰਸਿੱਖ, ਉੱਚ ਕੋਟੀ ਦੇ ਕੀਰਤਨੀਏ, ਲੋਭ-ਮੋਹ-ਹੰਕਾਰ ਤੋਂ ਰਹਿਤ ਕੋਈ ਵਿਰਲਾ ਹੀ ਲੱਭੇਗਾ।

ਦਰਸਾਉਂਦੀ ਰਹਿੰਦੀ ਹੈ।

ਨਵੀਂ ਦਿੱਲੀ
15 ਸਤੰਬਰ 1980		 English (Meaning Translation)

**Blessing**

That you have decided to write the biography of your father, Bhai Hira Singh Ji, is highly commendable. This biography is of such a revered Gursikh, whose life will provide light to every Sikh. Such a guileless servant, a perfect Gursikh, a Kirtan performer of the highest caliber, free from greed, attachment, and ego, is rarely found.

Waheguru sends such noble souls only occasionally through His grace for the benefit of common people, who leave their stamp, which continues to show its effect forever.

The immense effort you have put in and all the material you have collected is also a favor to the Panth. Spending so much, undertaking so many tours, and gathering all this from various places—this is your great labor and an act of benevolence for the Panth. By reading this biography, Sikhs will continue to benefit, and it will continue to provide light for them to lead their conduct as Gursikhs. I congratulate you.

6-A Ring Road, **Hukam Singh**
New Delhi Former Speaker Lok Sabha
15 September 1980 Former Governor Rajasthan
Founder,
Sri Guru Granth Sahib Vidya Kendra,
New Delhi

Notes
- Corrected likely OCR word: "ਨਿਰਸੋਲਕ" -> "ਨਿਰਸਵਾਰਥ" (context implies selfless/guileless).
- Corrected likely OCR word: "ਇਰ" -> "ਇਹ" (this).
Page 0004
ਜਾਣ ਪਛਾਣ

ਰੁਰਪੁਰਵਾਸੀ ਭਾਈ ਸਾਹਿਬ ਭਾਈ ਹੀਰਾ ਸਿੰਘ ਜੀ ਦੇ ਜੀਵਨ ਸਮਾਚਾਰ ਲਿਖ ਕੇ, ਉਨ੍ਹਾਂ
ਟੇ ਸਪੁੱਤਰ ਤੇ ਮੇਰੇ ਅਜ਼ੀਜ਼ ਮੇਜਰ ਬਲਵੰਤ ਸਿੰਘ ਨੇ ਜੋ ਇਸ ਨਿਰਮਾਣ ਪੰਥ ਸੈਵਕ ਦੀ ਯਾਦ
ਤਾਜ਼ਾ ਕੀਤੀ ਹੈਂ, ਇਹ ਬੜਾ ਸ਼ਲਾਘਾ ਯੋਗ ਉਂਦਮ ਹੈ। _
ਭਾਈ ਸਾਹਿਬ ਦਾ ਅਮੋਲਕ ਕੀਰਤਨ ਸੁਣਨ ਦਾ ਤੇ ਰਸ ਮਾਣਨ ਦਾ ਕਾਫ਼ੀ ਅਵਸਰ ਮੌਟੂ
ਪਾਉਂਦੇ ਸਨ। ਮੈਨੂੰ ਬਹੁਤ ਸਾਰੇ ਪੰਜਾਬੀ ਵਿੱਚ ਧਾਰਮਿਕ ਤੇ ਸਿਆਸੀ ਵਖਿਆਨ ਸੁਣਨ ਦੇ
ਅਵਸਰ ਮਿਲੇ ਹਨ। ਪਰ ਜੋ ਅਸਰ ਭਾਈ ਹੀਰਾ ਸਿੰਘ ਜੀ ਦੀ ਕਥਨੀ ਵਿੱਚ ਹੁੰਦਾ ਸੀ, ਮੈਂ ਹੁਣ
ਤਕ ਕਿਸੇ ਹੋਰ ਦੇ ਵਿੱਚ ਨਹੀਂ ਤੱਕਿਆ। ਇਹ ਸਿਰਫ਼ ਉਨ੍ਹਾਂ ਦੀ ਜ਼ਬਾਨ ਦੀ ਕਰਾਮਾਤ ਹੀ ਨਹੀਂ
ਸੀ, ਸਗੋਂ ਉਨ੍ਹਾਂ ਦੇ ਹਿਰਦੇ ਅੰਦਰ ਗੁਰਬਾਣੀ ਤੇ ਸਿੱਖ ਇਤਿਹਾਸ ਦਾ ਜੋ ਪ੍ਰਭਾਵ ਸੀ, ਉਸੇ ਦਾ
ਹੀ ਉਹ ਪ੍ਰਗਟਾਵਾ ਕਰਦੇ ਸਨ। ਇਸ ਪੁਸਤਕ ਵਿੱਚ ਮੈਨੂੰ ਜੋ ਨਵੀਆਂ ਗੱਲਾਂ ਪਤਾ ਲੱਗੀਆਂ
ਹਨ, ਉਹ ਉਨ੍ਹਾਂ ਦੇ ਛੋਟੇ ਹੁੰਦਿਆਂ ਦੇ ਜੀਵਨ ਬਾਬਤ ਹਨ। ਸ਼ੁਰੂ ਤੋਂ ਹੀ ਉਨ੍ਹਾਂ ਨੇ ਜੋ ਸੇਵਾ ਤੇ
ਸਿਮਰਨ ਦੀਆਂ ਘਾਲਾਂ ਘਲੀਆਂ ਹਨ, ਉਨ੍ਹਾਂ ਦੇ ਫਲ ਸਰੂਪ ਉਹੀ ਕੁਝ ਉਨ੍ਹਾਂ ਦੇ ਕੀਰਤਨ ਅਤੇ
ਕਥਨੀ ਰਾਹੀਂ ਸੰਗਤਾਂ ਦੇ ਸਾਹਮਣੇ ਆਇਆ।
ਜੀ ਬਾਰੇ ਪ੍ਰਾਚੀਨ ਅਖ਼ਬਾਰਾਂ ਵਿੱਚ ਖੋਜ ਕੇ ਤੇ ਉਨ੍ਹਾਂ ਦੇ ਸਮਕਾਲੀਆਂ ਨਾਲ ਸੰਪਰਕ ਕਰਕੇ,
ਪੁਸਤਕ ਸੰਪਾਦਨ ਕਰਨ ਦਾ ਜੋ ਉਦਮ ਕੀਤਾ ਹੈ, ਇੱਕ ਵਡਮੁੱਲੀ ਇਤਿਹਾਸਕ ਸੇਵਾ ਕੀਤੀ ਹੈ।
ਇਸ ਦੇ ਪ੍ਰਕਾਸ਼ਿਤ ਹੋਣ ਨਾਲ ਉਸ ਨਿਸ਼ਕਾਮ ਸੇਵਕ ਦੀ ਜੀਵਨੀ, ਨਾ ਸਿਰਫ਼ ਉਨ੍ਹਾਂ ਦੀ
ਯਾਦਗਾਰ ਬਣ ਗਈ ਹੈ, ਸਗੋਂ ਪੰਥ ਦੇ ਪ੍ਰਚਾਰ-ਇਤਿਹਾਸ 'ਚ ਸ਼ਲਾਘਾ ਯੋਗ ਵਾਧਾ ਹੋਇਆ ਹੈ
ਤੇ ਐਸੀਆਂ ਅਨੇਕਾਂ ਮਹੱਤਵਪੂਰਨ ਘਟਨਾਵਾਂ ਉਜਾਗਰ ਹੋਈਆਂ ਹਨ, ਜੋ ਕਿ ਇੱਕ ਆਦਰਸ਼ਕ
ਪ੍ਰਚਾਰਕ ਦੇ ਜੀਵਨ ਤੋਂ ਪ੍ਰਰਣਾ ਲੈਣ ਦਾ ਵਸੀਲਾ ਬਣ ਸਕਦੀਆਂ ਹਨ। ਮੈਂ ਇਸ ਸਫ਼ਲ ਯਤਨ		 English (Meaning Translation)

**Introduction**

By writing the life events of the late Bhai Sahib Bhai Hira Singh Ji, his eldest son and my dear Major Balwant Singh has refreshed the memory of this humble servant of the Panth; this is a highly praiseworthy endeavor.

[I] had ample opportunity to listen to and enjoy the precious Kirtan of Bhai Sahib. I have had opportunities to listen to many religious and political lectures in Punjabi. But the effect that was present in Bhai Hira Singh Ji's speech, I have not seen in anyone else till now. This was not just a miracle of his tongue, but rather the influence of Gurbani and Sikh History within his heart, of which he was a manifestation.

The new things I have learned in this book are regarding his childhood life. The toil of service (Seva) and remembrance (Simran) that he undertook from the very beginning, as a fruit of that, the same appeared before the congregations through his Kirtan and speech.

By searching through ancient newspapers about him and contacting his contemporaries to compile this book, a valuable historical service has been performed. With its publication, the biography of that selfless servant has not only become his memorial, but there has also been a praiseworthy addition to the preaching history of the Panth. Many such significant events have come to light which can become a source of inspiration from the life of an ideal preacher. I [congratulate] this successful effort.

Notes
- Corrected likely OCR word: "ਰੁਰਪੁਰਵਾਸੀ" -> "ਗੁਰਪੁਰਵਾਸੀ" (Late/Deceased).
- Corrected likely OCR word: "ਟੇ" -> "ਦੇ" (of).
- Corrected likely OCR word: "ਜਾ" -> "ਜਾਦੂ" (magic/spell) - implied from context "influence".

ਪਰਵਾਸੀ ਭਾਈ ਸਾਹਿਬ ਭਾਈ ਹੀਰਾ ਸਿੰਘ ਜੀ ਦੇ ਜੀਵਨ ਸਮਾਚਾਰ ਲਿਖ ਕੇ, ਉਨਾ
ਹ ਮਤਰ ਤੇ ਮੇਰੇ ਅਜ਼ੀਜ਼ ਮੇਜਰ ਬਲਵੰਤ ਸਿੰਘ ਨੇ ਜੋ ਇਸ ਨਿਰਮਾਣ ਪੰਥ ਸੈਵਕ ਦੀ ਯਾਦ
ਭਾਈ ਸਾਰਿਬ ਦਾ ਅਮੋਲਕ ਕੀਰਤਨ ਸੁਣਨ ਦਾ ਤੇ ਰਸ ਮਾਣਨ ਦਾ ਕਾਫ਼ੀ ਅਵਸਰ ਮੰਦੇ
ਮਿਲਿਆ ਹੈ ਤੇ ਇਸ ਪੁਸਤਕ ਨੂੰ ਪੜ੍ਹਦਿਆਂ ਉਹ ਸਾਰਾ ਨਜ਼ਾਰਾ ਮੇਰੇ ਸਾਹਮਣੇ ਆਇਆ ਹੈ ਕਿ
ਕਿਸ ਤਰ੍ਹਾਂ ਉਹ ਸੰਗਤ ਉੱਤੇ ਆਪਣੇ ਕੀਰਤਨ ਅਤੇ ਕਥਨੀ ਦੁਆਰਾ ਇੱਕ ਜਾ ਦਾ
ਪਾਉਂਦੇ ਸਨ। ਮੈਨੂੰ ਬਹੁਤ ਸਾਰੇ ਪੰਜਾਬੀ ਵਿੱਚ ਧਾਰਮਿਕ ਤੇ ਸਿਆਸੀ ਵਖਿਆਨ ਖਲ ਦਾ
ਅਫਸਰ ਮਿਲੋ ਹਨ । ਪੁਰ ਜੋ ਅਸਰ ਭਾਈ ਹੀਰਾ ਸਿੰਘ ਜੀ ਦੀ ਕਥਨੀ ਵਿੱਚ ਹੁੰਦਾ ਸੀ, ਮਂ ਚਣੇ
ਤਕ ਕਿਸੇ ਹੋਰ ਦੇ ਵਿੱਚ ਨਹੀਂ ਤੱਕਿਆ। ਇਹ ਸਿਰਫ਼ ਉਨ੍ਹਾਂ ਦੀ ਜ਼ਬਾਨ ਦੀ ਕਰਾਮਾਤ ਹੀਂ ਨਹੀਂ
ਸੀ, ਸਗਂ ਉਨ੍ਹਾਂ ਦੇ ਹਿਰਦੇ ਅੰਦਰ ਗੁਰਬਾਣੀ ਤੇ ਸਿੱਖ ਇਤਿਹਾਸ ਦਾ ਜੋ ਪ੍ਰਭਾਵ ਸੀ, ਉਸੇ ਦਾ
ਰੀ ਉਹ ਪ੍ਰਗਟਾਵਾ ਕਰਦੇ ਸਨ। ਇਸ ਪੁਸਤਕ ਵਿੱਚ ਮੈਨੂੰ ਜੋ ਨਵੀਆਂ ਗੱਲਾਂ ਪਤਾ ਲਗੀਆਂ
ਹਨ; ਉਹ ਉਨ੍ਹਾਂ ਦੇ ਛੋਟੇ ਹੁੰਦਿਆਂ ਦੇ ਜੀਵਨ ਬਾਬਤ ਹਨ। ਸੁਰੂ ਤੋਂ ਹੀ ਉਨ੍ਹਾਂ ਨੇ ਜੋ ਸੇਵਾ ਤੇ
ਸਿਮਰਨ ਦੀਆਂ ਘਾਲਾਂ ਘਲੀਆਂ ਹਨ, ਉਨ੍ਹਾਂ ਦੇ ਫਲ ਸਰੂਪ ਉਹੀ ਕੁਝ ਉਨ੍ਹਾਂ ਦੇ ਕੀਰਤਨ ਅਤੇ
ਕਥਨੀ ਰਾਹੀਂ ਸੰਗਤਾਂ ਦੇ ਸਾਹਮਣੇ ਆਇਆ।
ਇਸ ਦੇ ਪ੍ਰਕਾਸ਼ਿਤ ਹੋਣ ਨਾਲ ਉਸ ਨਿਸ਼ਕਾਮ ਸੇਵਕ ਦੀ ਜੀਵਨੀ, ਨਾ ਸਿਰਫ਼ ਉਨ੍ਹਾਂ ਦੀ
ਯਾਦਗਾਰ ਬਣ ਗਈ ਹੈ, ਸਗੋਂ ਪੰਥ ਦੇ ਪ੍ਰਚਾਰ-ਇਤਿਹਾਸ 'ਚ ਸ਼ਲਾਘਾ ਯੋਗ ਵਾਧਾ ਹੋਇਆ ਹੈ
ਤੇ ਐਸੀਆਂ ਅਨੇਕਾਂ ਮਹੱਤਵਪੂਰਨ ਘਟਨਾਵਾਂ ਉਜਾਗਰ ਹੋਈਆਂ ਹਨ, ਜੋ ਕਿ ਇੱਕ ਆਦਰਸ਼ਕ
ਪ੍ਰਚਾਰਕ ਦੇ ਜੀਵਨ ਤੋਂ ਪ੍ਰੇਰਣਾ ਲੈਣ ਦਾ ਵਸੀਲਾ ਬਣ ਸਕਦੀਆਂ ਹਨ। ਮੈਂ ਇਸ ਸਫ਼ਲ ਯਤਨ
॥੨]੭
12 ਕਸਤੂਰਬਾ ਮਾਰਗ ਉੱਜਲ ਸਿੰਘ
2 ਸਤੰਬਰ 1980 ਪੰਜਾਬ ਅਤੇ ਮਦਰਾਸ		 English (Meaning Translation)

**Introduction**

By writing the life events of the late Bhai Sahib Bhai Hira Singh Ji, his [son] and my dear Major Balwant Singh has refreshed the memory of this humble servant of the Panth.

[I] have had ample opportunity to listen to and enjoy the precious Kirtan of Bhai Sahib. Reading this book, the whole scene has come before my eyes of how he used to cast a spell over the congregation through his Kirtan and speech. I have had opportunities to listen to many religious and political lectures in Punjabi. But the effect that was present in Bhai Hira Singh Ji's speech, I have not seen in anyone else till now. This was not just a miracle of his tongue, but rather the influence of Gurbani and Sikh History within his heart, of which he was a manifestation.

The new things I have learned in this book are regarding his childhood life. The toil of service (Seva) and remembrance (Simran) that he undertook from the very beginning, as a fruit of that, the same appeared before the congregations through his Kirtan and speech.

With its publication, the biography of that selfless servant has not only become his memorial, but there has also been a praiseworthy addition to the preaching history of the Panth. Many such significant events have come to light which can become a source of inspiration from the life of an ideal preacher. I [congratulate] this successful effort.

12 Kasturba Marg **Ujjal Singh**
2 September 1980 (Former Governor) Punjab and Madras

ਟਾਅਰਆ 77.		 English (Meaning Translation)

**Preface**
(First Edition)

Many such humble and virtuous men have passed through the Sikh community who preached the religion, whose life achievements could create glorious traditions for the community, and whose biographies could serve as a lighthouse for future generations. But...

Many Gursikhs sacrificed their all—wealth, virtues, and personal health—to awaken the sleeping community after the fall of the Sikh Raj. If the accounts of their services do not come into written form today, then after another half-century, their memory or even their names and addresses will be lost forever.

Among such God-oriented Gursikhs and devoted servants, one name is that of the humble servant of the Panth, 'Bhai Sahib Bhai Hira Singh Ji Ragi', who performed tireless service for the growth of the Panth in every aspect—religious, social, and educational—in his time.

Many efforts were made to write a complete biography of Bhai Sahib, but they could not reach completion. First of all, after his departure for the Guru's Abode, in September 1926, Giani Hira Singh Dard (1889-1965), the editor of the monthly journal 'Phulwari', asked the author of these lines (who was then only a First Year student at Khalsa College) about some circumstances regarding Bhai Sahib. He published an article in the October 1926 issue under the title 'Crown Jewel of Sikh Preachers' along with a photo of him, and asked me to research and bring detailed news. Along with this, he also gave an indication at the end of his article about publishing a full biography in this hope. But this could not happen.

In the year 1931-32, Sriman Bhai Sahib Bhai Vir Singh Ji ordered me: "If you can find any diaries or handwritten notes of Bhai Hira Singh Ji, bring them to us." When I went to my village Faruka during the next summer vacations, I searched every corner of the house and found a daily journal written in his own hand, which was in the form of a register. In this, events from his adolescence up to approximately the year 1902-03 were recorded. After this... [text cuts off]

- Corrected likely OCR word: "ਮੌਟੂ" -> "ਮੈਨੂੰ" (me/I) - context fix.

ਮਰੰਮਲ ਜੀਵਨ ਅੰਕਿਤ ਕੀਤਾ ਜਾਵੇ। ਅਸਾਂ ਉਨ੍ਹਾਂ ਨੂੰ ਮਾਇਕ ਸੇਵਾ ਲਈ ਭਰੋਸਾ ਦਿਵਾਇਆ
ਦੀਆਂ ਅੱਖਾਂ ਤੇ ਸਿਹਤ ਨੇ ਸਾਥ ਨਾ ਦਿੱਤਾ।
ਸੰਨ 1967 ਵਿੱਚ ਮੈਨ ਸ੍ਰੀ ਅੰਮ੍ਰਿਤਸਰ, ਚੀਫ਼ ਖ਼ਾਲਸਾ ਦੀਵਾਨ ਦੇ ਦਫ਼ਤਰ ਵਿੱਚ ਜਾਣੇ ਦਾ
(੬੯ ਨਲ 7
ਣੂਨੀਕਾ - 7		 English (Meaning Translation)

[...Previous text cut off] ...found his other diaries, which were up to 1925. In these, [there was] much...

Taking the aforementioned register and diaries, I appeared in the presence of Bhai Sahib Bhai Vir Singh Ji. He handed over all that material to Dr. Balbir Singh Ji. Some time later, Doctor Sahib called me and said, "Clean [this]... and organize it under different subject headings."

Due to the struggle for livelihood, I could not do this. [I said], "I have kept the daily journal and the news written from the diaries safe with me... This is the property of the Panth; hand it over to us so that the life of this unique servant of the Panth can be recorded." So Mata Ji handed over that register and the bundle of [diaries] to Bhai Sudh Singh Ji. This is perhaps a mention of 1944.

But God's will was such that during the partition of the country, this entire bundle remained at Bhai Sudh Singh Ji's house in Sargodha. [It was lost].

Then, on the occasion of the 25th death anniversary of Bhai Hira Singh Ji, Sriman Bhai Sahib Bhai Vir Singh Ji published a special [issue] of 'Khalsa Samachar' on 30 August 1951. Many loved ones sent their articles and poems. These articles were so numerous [that] another special issue of 'Khalsa Samachar' was published on 28 August 1952...

Since then, almost every year on Bhai Sahib's death anniversary, articles by one or another Gurmukh have continued to be published. The largest share among these belongs to Bhai Sahib Bhai Sudh Singh Ji, who had immense love for Bhai Hira Singh Ji. Reading about the life events and Panthic services of Bhai Sahib in these articles, I began to feel the [value] of my heritage, and a desire arose to preserve this heritage!

[It was decided] that a complete biography should be recorded. We assured him of financial service... [but] his eyes and health did not support him.

In 1967, I had an occasion to go to the office of the Chief Khalsa Diwan in Sri Amritsar...

ਅਰਦਾਸਾ ਸੋਧ ਕੈ ਆਰੰਭ ਕਰਨਾ, ਬੱਚੀ ਦੇ ਚਲਾਣੇ (1922) ਉੱਤੇ ਘਰ ਵਿੱਚ ਰੋਣ-ਧੌਟ ਨ
6 - #ਸੰਲਕ ਹੀਰਾ
”ੇ		 English (Meaning Translation)

...opportunity I got, where reading the details of Bhai Hira Singh Ji's life and his services to Conferences and Sikh Ashrams published in the Educational Committee's 'Silver Jubilee Book' (1935) and 'Golden Jubilee Book' (1958), my eyes were opened. I felt astonished joy, and my enthusiasm increased further.

Upon the loss of the material written in Bhai Hira Singh Ji's own hand, I observed that the events of Bhai Sahib's preaching field are found mostly in 'Khalsa Samachar'. His relations with this weekly remained deep from its inception till the end. Since November 1899, when this paper started, details regarding Bhai Hira Singh Ji's selfless service for Amrit Sanchar (Sikh baptism) and Gur-Maryada Anand Karaj (Sikh wedding ceremony) are found in it.

I examined some old files of Khalsa Samachar at 60 Lawrence Road, Amritsar, and [others] by going to Sahit Kendra Dehradun.

Here, when I read the three articles published in the September month of the 1926 Khalsa Samachar file upon Bhai Sahib's passing (which were published in the issues of 9, 23, and 30 September 1926), I burst into tears and realized: "What! He was such a great personality and we didn't even know this much!"

"I opened the treasure of my father and grandfather,
And I found the storehouse of jewels."
(G.G.S. Ang 186)

This Guru-Vak (Guru's word) became visibly true.

The photo of late Giani Hira Singh Dard with Bhai Sahib was obtained from the old issues of 'Phulwari' from Jalandhar after a long search.
I read the 'Khalsa' newspapers of the last decades of the previous century by going to the Bhai Ditt Singh Library in Ferozepur.

As far as my personal knowledge is concerned, I submit that at the time of Bhai Sahib's passing, my age was 15 years. Although he got very little time to stay at home, he used to take us children along to many Diwans and Conference congregations. Therefore, looking at his life from childhood... his life according to Gurmat, starting every task by taking the shelter of Guru Maharaj and offering Ardas... not crying or wailing at home upon the death of his daughter (1922)...

- Corrected likely OCR word: "ਸ਼ੁਸ਼ੀ" -> "ਖੁਸ਼ੀ" (happiness).
- Corrected likely OCR word: "ਪਟ" -> "ਪਰ" (But/Upon) - inferred context.

ਤਾਂ ਪਤਾ ਲੱਗਾ ਕਿ ਸ੍ਰੀਮਾਨ ਭਾਈ ਸਾਹਿਬ ਭਾਈ ਵੀਰ ਸਿੰਘ ਜੀ ਨੇ ਇਹ ਲਫ਼ਜ਼ ਭਾਈ ਹੀਰਾ ਸਿੰਘ
ਜੀ ਲਈ ਕਿਉ ਵਰਤਿਆ ਸੀ।
ਉਨ੍ਹਾਂ ਇਸ ਲੇਖ ਵਿੱਚ ਇੱਕ ਥਾਂ ਇਉਂ ਲਿਖਿਆ ਹੈ : 'ਭਾਈ ਹੀਰਾ ਸਿੰਘ ਜੀ ਵਿੱਚ ਧਰਮ
ਭਾਵ ਸੀ, ਸਿਮਰਨ ਦਾ ਸ਼ੌਕ ਸੀ, ਬਾਣੀ ਨਾਲ ਅੰਦਰੋਂ ਰੁਚੀ ਸੀ, ਬਾਣੀ ਦੇ ਭਾਵ ਤੇ ਸਤਿਗੁਰਾਂ
ਦੇ ਜੀਵਨ ਦੀ ਸਮਝ ਵਿੱਚ ਕਵਿਤਾ ਦੇ ਦਰਜੇ ਦਾ ਅਨੁਭਵ ਸੀ, ਫੇਰ ਕੀਰਤਨ ਦੇ ਨਾਲ ਕਮਾਲ
ਸੀ ਫ਼ਸਾਹਤ ਦਾ; ਕਥਨੀ ਵਿੱਚ ਬਰਕਤ ਸੀ - ਦਾਤ ਸਾਂਈ ਦੀ - ਪਰ ਅੰਦਰਲੇ ਧਰਮ ਭਾਵੇ
ਦੇ ਨਕਸ਼ ਉਸ ਦੇ ਕਥਨ ਵਿੱਚ ਕਲਾ-ਕੌਸ਼ਲ ਦਾ ਕਮਾਲ ਦਿਖਾਲਦੇ ਸਨ... ਰ
ਰਾਈ ਹੀਰਾ ਸਿੰਘ ਜੀ ਦੇ ਮੁੱਢਲੇ ਸਮਾਚਾਰ ਤੇ ਉਨ੍ਹਾਂ ਦੇ ਪਿਤਾ-ਪਿਤਾਮਾ ਬਾਰੇ ਕੁਝ ਤਾਂ ਅਸਾਂ
ਹੋ ਸਨ ਅਤੇ ਵਿਆਹ (1894) ਤੋਂ ਬਾਅਦ ਦੇ ਜੀਵਨ-ਕਾਲ ਬਾਰੇ ਸਾਡੀ ਮਾਤਾ, ਸ੍ਰੀਮਤੀ
ਪੇਮ ਕੌਰ ਜੀ ਬੁਤ ਕੁਝ ਦੱਸਿਆ ਕਰਦੇ ਸਨ, ਪਰ ਇਨ੍ਹਾਂ ਨੂੰ ਤਰਤੀਬਵਾਰ ਕਰਨ ਲਈ, ਸੱਠ

"7" (ਅਲ ੭		 English (Meaning Translation)

...narrating the stories of martyrdom in the Diwans to fill the congregation with zeal for the agitation; giving visible Darshan of Guru Nanak Sahib in the Diwans at Sri Nankana Sahib on Katik Purnima; doing Kirtan in solitude sitting on sand dunes with a small harmonium at night when visiting home at Faruka; and remaining engrossed in meditation during the day—these are such events that are etched on my mind.

In 1924, I had the opportunity to observe his life closely by staying with him for about two months in Koh Mari and Dumel etc., and in the summer of 1925 in Shimla. And then I had the good fortune of serving him during the last 5 months of 1926... [my duty] was to recite prayers. Apart from this, I also got the opportunity to serve with my own hands.

In these very days, upon passing Matric in June 1926, you sent me to Amritsar to get admission in Khalsa College and ordered me to first go and have Darshan of Sriman Bhai Sahib Bhai Vir Singh Ji at Lawrence Road. Accordingly, reaching there, Sri Bhai Sahib Ji kept me with him, and the next day when Principal Gopala Rao came to see him, he handed me over to him. He took me with him to the college and completed the admission formalities. I came back to Lawrence Road. In the evening after tea, when he was leaving for Majitha House to play badminton sitting in his Victoria carriage, he took me along too. I sat on the floor of the carriage at his feet, but he caught me by the arm and lifted me up, hugged me to his chest with love, and seating me on the seat opposite him said, "Why are you sitting on the floor? Do you know whose son you are? Your father is a 'Genius', a 'Genius'." At that time I did not even know the full meaning of this word, but this word 'Genius' kept echoing in my ears all my life.

...And now, half a century after his passing, when I read the main article 'Empty Space in the Panth' in the Khalsa Samachar issue of 30 September 1926, I realized why Sriman Bhai Sahib Bhai Vir Singh Ji had used this word for Bhai Hira Singh Ji.

He has written in one place in this article: "In Bhai Hira Singh Ji, there was a sense of religion, a passion for Simran, an inner love for Gurbani; in the understanding of the essence of Gurbani and the life of the Satgurus, he had the experience of the level of poetry; then with Kirtan there was a mastery of eloquence; there was blessing in his speech - a gift of the Lord - but the features of his inner religious emotion showed the perfection of art and skill in his speech..."

Regarding the early life of Bhai Hira Singh Ji and his father and grandfather, we [knew some facts]... and about the life after his marriage (1894), our mother, Srimati Prem Kaur Ji used to tell us a lot, but to organize these, in 1962-63, we recorded them on tape by asking her in the form of questions and answers.

੮“ .ਐੱ ਹ> '
੍		 English (Meaning Translation)

[...kept] safe till today. Then upon coming to Yamuna Nagar... I met **Bhai Sant Singh Ji Khurana** (1877-1970) [who was from his village Faruka]... and had acquired the education of Gur-History from the top scholar of Gurmat **Bhai Mahna Singh Ji** (1815-1905) at the Dharamsala of Faruka.

Regarding Bhai Sahib's personal life, many events were learned from **Sri Sant Nishchal Singh Ji Maharaj** (1882-1978). Coincidentally, 4-5 days before Sant Ji passed away, when I went to see him, he patted my back as always and said, "Seeing you reminds us of Bhai Hira Singh." He narrated 4-5 incidents about Bhai Sahib. Naturally, at that time Giani Mohar Singh Ji Narang, Editor of 'Gur Sandesh' was also present there; he published all these events in the next issue of 'Gur Sandesh', October 1978.

Apart from this, whatever I could obtain by meeting Bhai Sahib's contemporaries and other friends or through correspondence, I have tried to present in this book. I am grateful to all such gentlemen who helped...
In this regard, I feel it necessary to make special mention of the late **Bhai Pradhan Singh Ji Ragi** (Jatha Bhai Sudh Singh Ji). When he [learned] about the book, he was so impressed that he started writing me letters repeatedly to publish the complete biography soon. Whenever he remembered an event, he used to write and send it to me. I also kept going to Delhi specially to meet him.
The last time when I went and showed him the complete manuscript in May 1979 and read out some parts to him, he was very pleased and said, "If this is printed and ready in my lifetime, I will be very happy." But alas! His wish could not be fulfilled and he departed for the Guru's Abode on 6-8-79.

In the preparation of this manuscript, my younger brother **Major Agyapal Singh**... Air Vice Marshal Manjit Singh, S. Manmohan Singh Chief Engineer, Major General Surjit Singh and Brigadier Surinder Singh gave me full cooperation.

In the end, I ask forgiveness from the readers for my errors.


220-R, Model Town **Balwant Singh Major**
Yamuna Nagar
2 September 1980

ਸਾਬਕਾ ਸਪੀਕਰ ਲੋਕ ਸਭਾ ਦੀ ਸਰਪਰਸਤੀ ਹੇਠ ਭਾਈ ਹੀਰਾ ਸਿੰਘ ਜੀ ਦੀ ਜਨਮ ਸ਼ਤਾਬਦੀ

ਦੀ ਗਿਣਤੀ ਵਿੱਚ ਸੰਗਤਾਂ ਨੇ ਹਾਜ਼ਰੀ ਭਰੀ ਸੀ। 'ਸਿੰਘ ਸਭਾ ਪਤ੍ਰਿਕਾ', 'ਅਜੀਤ', ਅਕਾਲੀ
ਟਾਈਮਜ਼', 'ਪੰਜਾਬੀ ਟ੍ਰਿਬਿਊਨ', ਖ਼ਾਲਸਾ ਸਮਾਚਾਰ' ਤੇ 'ਖ਼ਾਲਸਾ ਐਡਵੋਕੇਟ' ਦੇ ਵਿਸ਼ੇਸ਼ ਅੰਕ
ਪੁਕਾਸ਼ਿਤ ਹੋਏ ਸਨ। ਇਨ੍ਹਾਂ ਵਿੱਚੋਂ ਅਤੇ 50ਵੀਂ ਬਰਸੀ ਅਤੇ ਜਨਮ ਸ਼ਤਾਬਦੀ ਜਾਂ ਉਸ ਤੋਂ ਪਿੱਛੋਂ
ਛਪੇ ਲੇਖਾਂ ਵਿੱਚੋਂ ਕੁਝ ਚੋਣਵੇ ਲੇਖ ਤੇ ਕਵਿਤਾਵਾਂ ਇਸ ਪੁਸਤਕ ਦੇ ਅਖੀਰ ਵਿੱਚ ਦਿੱਤੀਆਂ ਹਨ।
ਪੁਸਤਕ ਦਾ ਆਕਾਰ ਵੱਡਾ ਹੋਣ ਦੀ ਮਜਬੂਰੀ ਕਾਰਨ, ਇਹ ਲੇਖ ਸੰਖੇਪ ਕਰਕੇ ਛਾਪੇ ਗਏ ਹਨ।
ਇੱਕੋ ਲੇਖਾਂ ਤੋਂ ਛੁੱਟ ਸਾਰੇ ਲੇਖ ਤੇ ਕਵਿਤਾਵਾਂ ਭਾਈ ਸਾਹਿਬ ਦੇ ਸਮਕਾਲੀਆਂ ਦੀਆਂ ਲਿਖਤਾਂ
ਹਨ|

ਰਾ		 English (Meaning Translation)

**Preface**
(Second Edition)

...[The demand for the book] kept coming, so the order could not be fulfilled. Upon the insistence of some admirers, an effort was made to print the second edition. In this, some additions and many detailed [accounts have been included].
On the 25th death anniversary of Bhai Hira Singh Ji, two special issues of 'Khalsa Samachar' were published in 1951 and 1952. And since all this writing was by the contemporaries of Bhai Sahib, therefore their eye-witnessed events have been used in 'Amolak Hira'.

On 2 September 1976, Bhai Sahib's 50th death anniversary was observed at the Khalsa High School established by him in Faruka (now at Ambala Cantonment). On this occasion, 'Bhai Hira Singh Model School' was opened there, and scholarships were started in the big school in his name for students coming First and Second in Divinity in every class. For their permanent fund, money [was given] by Bhai Hira Singh Ji's family...

In November 1979, under the patronage of the late Sardar Hukam Singh Ji, former Speaker Lok Sabha, the Birth Centenary of Bhai Hira Singh Ji was celebrated with great devotion and enthusiasm by the Kendri Singh Sabha at Chandigarh. Here, thousands of Sangat from far and near attended. Special issues of 'Singh Sabha Patrika', 'Ajit', 'Akali Times', 'Punjabi Tribune', 'Khalsa Samachar' and 'Khalsa Advocate' were published.
Some selected articles and poems from these, and from those published after the 50th anniversary and birth centenary, have been given at the end of this book. Due to the compulsion of the book size becoming large, these articles have been printed in condensed form.
Except for one or two articles, all articles and poems are writings of Bhai Sahib's contemporaries.

250-R, Model Town, **Dass** (Servant/Humble),
1 December 1985 [Balwant Singh]

9=/		 English (Meaning Translation)

Our most respected father, Major Balwant Singh Ji, completed his worldly journey of [number] years on 7 May 2004 and departed for the Guru's Abode. He had a special love for this book. His younger brother, Major Agyapal Singh Ji, performed great service in reaching this book to the Sikh Sangats. He too had passed away in June 1999.

According to the desire of the family, a function is organized every year in the memory of Bhai Hira Singh Ji. In this, there has often been a demand that [this book be reprinted].
[Therefore], an effort has been made to print the book for the third time with [some] changes.

1138 Sector 33-C, **Dasre** (Servants/Humble),
1 September 2009 (Chairman, Bhai Hira Singh Memorial Trust)

% % % ਗੇ ਬੱ		 English (Meaning Translation)

...White turban, white scarf (dupatta) around the neck, and head tilted to one side; he [was] a symbol of humility and humbleness. Yes!
...There was immense passion for the preaching of Gursikhi and Gurbani, and the [field of] preaching was his... through his Kirtan and lectures, reaching the [corners] of the country to flourish the garden of Gursikhi - the great service that the True Guru took from Bhai Hira Singh Ji by His grace, it is hard to find its parallel.

Bhai Hira Singh Ji lived his whole life for others; every thought he had was for the welfare of others. Every step he took was for the welfare of others, and every effort and labor...

Bhai Hira Singh Ji's background was neither of any rich nor of any wealthy family, nor was his birthplace famous from any aspect. Born in an ordinary house in a very backward area, without any financial means, if he grew up to become famous in the Panth, and was so respected and loved, then there must be some such special quality in him which cannot be in ordinary men. Perhaps that is why upon his departure to the next world, the sincere Editor wrote in the main article of 'Khalsa Samachar': "Bhai Hira Singh Ji Ragi was among those special men who are not born always, rather special needs of the country and community give birth to them."

- Corrected likely OCR word: "ਜਾ" -> "ਦਾ" (of/was).

(੯
ਤਾ		 English (Meaning Translation)

Before starting the life story of Bhai Hira Singh Ji, it is very important to give the readers a little information about his birth land, so that... map comes before the eyes, where Bhai Sahib's birth took place, where he spent his childhood time and received education, and to raise the standard of educational and social life of which land he made many efforts.

Near the border of Jhang Shahpur in West Punjab (now Pakistan), a small town was settled, whose name 'Faruka' was based on a Muslim clan named 'Farooq' or caste. At the end of the nineteenth century, only four or five houses of 'Farookas' were left, and due to the ownership of most lands being with 'Kaliars', the chiefs of that area were 'Kaliars'.

In the time we are talking about, their chief was Allah Yar Kaliar. [He] was a God-fearing and noble man. Being the Zaildar of that whole area, he considered the population of [the area] as his subjects and shared in the joys and sorrows of the people.
His son was also a noble man, although he held good influence/awe.

With the arrival of canal and rail in the [area] and the colonization of Sargodha Bar, some [change came]. The railway station Silanwali was 9 miles away from Faruka. [To travel] from Faruka, there was no means other than camels or horses. In the [beginning of] the twentieth century, due to the labor of Bhai Hira Singh Ji, with the establishment of Khalsa High School, the road also became paved, and tumtums and tongas also started running.

[Whenever one mentions Faruka], the other name necessarily comes to the fore. Just as 'Bhai Hira Singh Ji Faruke Wale' or...

- Corrected likely OCR word: "ਪਛਮੀ" -> "West" (Punjab).

76 - ਅਸੋਲਕ ਲੋਨ `--------------------------------		 English (Meaning Translation)

...Faruka, Bhai Hira Singh Ji's [town].
As far as religious life is concerned, this was due to the labor and service-simran of the great men of the Seva Panthi Deras of West Punjab.
In the area of Jhang, there were many Deras of this sect, such as Shahpur, Mitha Tiwana, Nurpur Thal, Shah Jiwana, Jhang Maghiana, Kot Isa Shah and Lallu etc.
Due to the high and pure living and earning of Naam by their Saints and Mahants, [the spread of] Sikhism used to happen naturally.

In Faruka also, there was an abode of 'Bhai Jeet Singh', blessed by this sect. Bhai Jeet Singh Ji, where he was a treasure of service and Simran, was also a great scholar. He started the system of Gurmukhi-Gurbani education in his Dharamsala... and similarly by establishing Dharamsalas in nearby villages, he spread Sikhism and established centers of Gurmukhi-Gurbani education. In these Dharamsalas, the visiting travelers also received food, water, and rest. Then bringing congregations from far and wide to Faruka, Bhai Jeet Singh Ji used to hold Satsang and flow the stream of Katha-Kirtan.

Bhai Jeet Singh Ji is written as a supremely generous soul, celibate, and contented person. The awe of his saintliness was so established in the whole area that Hindus and Muslims alike respected him. Bhai Jeet Singh Ji's successor was Bhai Darbara Singh Ji. Ahead were Bhai Ganda Singh and then Bhai Jiwan Singh Ji. Their departure... happened in 1942 after living the age of [number] years.

The second disciple of Bhai Ganda Singh of the aforementioned lineage was **Bhai Mahna Singh Ji**. He built a separate abode by taking an open space in front of the aforementioned Dharamsala. Here, Langar was always ready and every call of the visitors was served. Bhai Mahna Singh Ji was very benevolent. He used to help the poor and widows/needy a lot.
The grain for [his] Langar was ground on hand-mills in houses...
Bhai Mahna Singh Ji was a very learned and virtuous man. In his Dharamsala, the Katha of... Suraj Prakash continued constantly. All Sikhs [received] Gurmukhi education [from him].

- Corrected likely OCR word: "ਪ੍ਰਣਾਲੀ" -> "system/tradition".

ਸਨਮ` ਭੂਮ - 77		 English (Meaning Translation)

...used to do. His demise happened in 1905 after living an age of about 80 years.

The disciple of Bhai Mahna Singh Ji was **Bhai Achhar Singh Ji**, who despite being blind (Netra-hin), was a scholar of high caliber. From his scholarship, one can guess the ability of Bhai Mahna Singh Ji, and also of his other disciples, among whom Bhai Hira Singh Ji was also included.

Bhai Achhar Singh Ji had built his separate abode in a 'Chubara' (room on the upper floor) at the end of the bazaar. And in this Dharamsala, the 'Dasam Granth' was also installed along with 'Sri Guru Granth Sahib'. Sri Guru Granth Sahib Ji was as if memorized by heart to him. [If someone read wrong], he would say "Yes! Why are you making a mistake, O one with eyes?" He used to perform Katha of Dasam Granth also.

In the beginning, many students of Khalsa High School Faruka received education from Bhai Achhar Singh Ji to prepare for the Giani examination. At that time the course used to be quite difficult. It included parts of Suraj Prakash, Bhagat Bani, Hanuman Natak and Vidya Sagar etc., but after taking education from him, students used to pass with good marks.

Bhai Achhar Singh Ji used to perform very melodious Kirtan with Dilruba/Saranda. His demise happened in 1943 after living an age of about 90 years.

Apart from the above three Seva Panthis, there was also a Dharamsala of an Udasi Mahatma, **Baba Sadhu Sachiar** in Faruka. This was famous as 'Baddi Dharamsala' (Big Dharamsala), perhaps because its Barandari and courtyard were quite spacious. Baba Ji's name was Sadhu Ram, but due to his words being true, he was popular as 'Sadhu Sachiar' (Truthful). It is said that he had come from the West with some disciples and settled here. Some time later, when Maharaja Ranjit Singh passed through the route of Faruka, Sahiwal on a campaign, he was extremely pleased to have Darshan of Baba Ji and listen to his Bachan (words). Maharaja Sahib [got a well dug] and his servants used to produce grain by farming for those coming and going to the Dharamsala. Until the beginning of the twentieth century, we have seen this well running ourselves.

Among the special devotees of Baba Sadhu Sachiar were gentlemen of Batra lineage, who took up the responsibility of service and maintenance of this abode after Baba Ji and [continued] the flow of Naam-Bani.

Notes

- Corrected likely OCR word: "ਨੇਤ੍ਹੀਨ" -> "Netra-hin" (Blind).

“5 - ਅਸਲਾ ਗੰਨਾ		 English (Meaning Translation)

**Baba Sahib Singh Ji Bedi** of Una and after him his sons also used to come to Faruka and preach in this very Dharamsala.
The recognition of this Gurdwara was due to the name of Baba Sadhu Sachiar who was a Mahapurush of spiritual earning/power and truth. All the weddings of the village used to take place here only.
In the light of the high and pure life of the Mahapurushas of these abodes, the residents of [Faruka] used to be very religious and God-fearing. They were guileless, simple-natured and contented men. Their dealings were clean and pure. The fraud, black market and deceit of today's era was not seen. [In the matter of] earning wealth...

**Social Life**
Apart from kinship, the rites and customs were also the same. Before the Singh Sabha movement, the same Brahmanical methods were prevalent for the rites of birth, death, marriage etc.

**Establishment of Singh Sabha:**
Due to the Singh Sabha movement running in the Panth, with the inspiration of Bhai Hira Singh Ji, **Sri Guru Singh Sabha Faruka** came into existence in the year 1897-98.
Bhai Bhagwan Singh Ji was appointed the Jathedar and Bhai Hazoor Singh Ji Khurana the Secretary of this Singh Sabha. This Sabha was first affiliated with 'Khalsa Diwan Lahore' and later in 1902 upon the establishment of 'Chief Khalsa Diwan' it got associated with it.

Bhai Hazoor Singh Ji Khurana was a classmate of Bhai Hira Singh Ji in childhood. He contributed significantly to the Singh Sabha Faruka. [Regarding]... Kanya Pathshala (Girls' School) and School, he [worked] with Bhai Hira Singh Ji... [They had] brotherly love for each other. He [served]... passed away in 1919 becoming a victim of the Influenza epidemic.

[In the beginning] there was great opposition to the Singh Sabha in the village and the Singh Sabhias were treated very badly... to the extent that the city dwellers did not even let them fill water from the wells... [If they] touched, then they would wash the rope to purify it and then fill their water.

There was no question of Anand Karaj (Sikh wedding) taking place with the 'Maryada' (Sikh code). The [elders] were adamant on this point that they would conduct weddings only through Bedi (Hindu ritual).

Notes
- Corrected likely OCR word: "ਫੈ" -> "Influenza" (Context: 1919 Epidemic).
- Corrected likely OCR word: "ਲੱਜ" -> "Lajj" (Rope used for well).

ਸ਼ਨਮ` ਭੂਆ - 2		 English (Meaning Translation)

**Bhai Hira Singh Ji**, who was a strong supporter of Gur-Maryada, [made efforts]... and this way established the tradition of Anand Karaj in the area.
Where the preachers used to come and preach in the Diwans, there many other virtuous scholars also used to visit... Saint Attar Singh Ji, Saint Sangat Singh Ji... Bhai [Vir?] Singh Ji, Saint Gurbakhsh Singh Ji etc. put their feet on this land.

As a result of these religious Diwans, and with the efforts of Bhai Hira Singh Ji, the Kanya Pathshala (Girls' School) in 1906 and Khalsa High School in 1908 came into existence in Faruka.
The influence of the activities of Singh Sabha Faruka was bound to be on the nearby villages. In Silanwali, Sahiwal etc., Singh Sabhas were established and religious Diwans started to be held. In every small village of the area, wherever Sikhs [lived]...
These gentlemen used to attend the religious Diwans of Faruka and every year many people used to partake Amrit. Abandoning the Brahmanical rites prevalent in the whole area, the Sangat started following the objectives of Singh Sabha. At many places, like in a village of rich moneylenders named 'Pahlad', Gurmatas were passed that all rites of death etc. be done according to Gurmat; flowers (ashes) should not be picked on death nor should they be taken to Haridwar, rather collecting all the skeletal remains they should be flown in the nearby flowing Jhelum river; Shradhs-Navratras and other such rituals should be abandoned etc. Apart from this, the devotees here formed a Jatha for selfless service, which used to [serve] in the [Diwans] of the area, like celebrating Gurpurabs etc. and performing the service of Akhand Path without any offering, rather eating Prasada (food) from their own home and reaching on their own horses/transport.

**Participation in Akali Movement and Gurdwara Reform Movement:**
Many of the youths of Faruka and the area reached Sri Amritsar during the time of Gurdwara Reform Movement and dedicated their services to the Panth, and courted arrests in Guru Ka Bagh and Jaito Morchas.

Notes
- Corrected likely OCR word: "ਪਰਵਾਰਕ" -> "supporter/advocate".
- Corrected likely OCR word: "ਫੁੱਲ" -> "Phul" (Ashes/Remains).

ਕਰਨਾ, ਆਪ ਦਾ ਨਿਤ ਕਰਮ ਸੀ। ਫਿਰ ਭਾਈ ਜੀਤ ਸਿੰਘ ਦੀ ਧਰਮਸਾਲ ਵਿੱਚ ਹਾਜ਼ਰੀ ਭਰਨੀ
ਤੇ ਸਰੀ ਗੁਰੂ ਗ੍ਰੰਥ ਸਾਹਿਬ ਜੀ ਦਾ ਪਾਠ-ਹੁਕਮ ਲੈ ਕੇ ਆਪਣੇ ਕਾਰੋਬਾਰ ਵਿੱਚ ਲੱਗਣਾ । ਧਰਮਸਾਲ
ਸੀ। ਮਾਤਾ ਜੀ ਬੜੇ ਗੁਰਮੁਖ ਤੇ ਸੰਤ ਸੇਵੀ ਸਨ, ਉਹ ਇਹ ਸੇਵਾ ਕਰਕੇ ਆਪਣਾ ਧੰਨ-ਭਾਗ
ਸਮਝਦੇ ਸਨ।

27 - ਅਨੌਲਲਾ ਫੰਡ		 English (Meaning Translation)

**Background**
We will start the mention of the father and grandfather of Bhai Hira Singh Ji from his Gurmukh beloved grandfather, **Bhai Jiwan Singh Ji**.

At the end of the Dharamsala street of Bhai Jeet Singh Ji, there was a small house where a Gurmukh hard-working Sikh used to live, whose auspicious name was Bhai Jiwan Singh. He was a famous gentleman in the area due to his Sikh character and Gurmat way of life.
To wake up in the last quarter of the night (early morning) and perform Nitnem and recitation of Sukhmani Sahib was his daily routine. Then he would attend Bhai Jeet Singh's Dharamsala and after taking the Hukam of Sri Guru Granth Sahib Ji, he would engage in his business... Mata Ji was a great Gurmukh and server of Saints; she considered herself fortunate by doing this service.

The name of Bhai Jiwan Singh Ji's father was **Baba Channan Singh** and grandfather's name was **Bhai Devi Das**. Baba Channan Singh, along with his two elder sons, Prem Singh and Jiwan Singh, used to do the business of transporting goods on camels to the East (Purb Desh). The third son, Bhai Kalhu Ram, used to look after the house. From Khewra [salt mines] in West Punjab... Jaggery, Cloth and other goods used to go to the West.

In the year of the mutiny of **1857**, when Baba Jiwan Singh Ji had come to the East country with his elder brother Baba Prem Singh, they suffered a lot of loss at that time. Like many other traders of the area, these two brothers also returned home after a long time. Baba Prem Singh then left home and settled in Patiala, but Baba Jiwan Singh remained in his own home [Faruka] and started the work of farming... near Faruka...

Two children were born in the house of Baba Jiwan Singh. The first boy [was born] in 1844... whose name was kept **Bhag Singh**. After this a son...
Baba Ji completed his life journey and passed away in the year 1893 after living an age of about 73 years.

- Corrected likely OCR word: "ਪੂਰਬ ਦੇਸ਼" -> East Country (Indicates UP/Delhi side relative to Punjab).

/#ਛੌਕੜ` - 2/		 English (Meaning Translation)

At this time [1893] his grandson Hira Singh born from his... was about 13 years old. Child Hira Singh enjoyed the love of his grandfather to the fullest and memorized Gurbani prayers sitting in his lap. Bhai Hira Singh Ji used to mention this himself.

The husband of his beloved Aunt (Bhua), **Bhai Jawahar Singh Ji**, was a very Gurmukh and sweet-spoken gentleman. Upon the colonization of Sargodha, he opened a cloth shop there, which ran well until the partition of the country. Bhua Ji passed away in 1947 in Sargodha itself after living an age of about 97 years, and Bhaiaya Jawahar Singh Ji settled in Faridkot with his family. Here he passed away in 1952 at the age of over 100 years.

Bhai Hira Singh Ji's maternal grandfather (Nana), **Bhai Bhag Singh Ji Gand**, was a reputed gentleman and a wealthy landlord of the area. His father, Bhai Sewa Singh Ji, was a very Gurmukh and pious man, and grandfather Sardar Jassa Singh, being a recognized leader of his area, was appointed a Sardar of the Khalsa Armies. He had great influence during the Sikh Raj.

The ownership of land was mostly with Muslims, but whatever land belonged to non-Muslims, the largest share of ancestral land belonged to Bhai Bhag Singh Ji Gand, which was on wells. When the canal came at the end of the nineteenth century, Bhai Bhag Singh Ji Gand purchased 29 squares (725 acres) of canal land five-six miles away from Faruka and settled his own village, which became famous as **Kot Bhai Bhag Singh**. Thus the influence and awe of Bhai Bhag Singh Ji increased even more. The Kaliars, before whom no one could raise their eyes, Bhai Bhag Singh Gand had the capacity to clash with them if needed.

The eldest daughter of Bhai Bhag Singh Ji Gand, **Srimati Sat Bharai**, had the honor of being the blessed mother of Bhai Hira Singh. Younger to her were three boys and four girls.

Bhai Hira Singh Ji's maternal uncles (Mama), Bhai Bhagwan Singh Ji (1864-1947), Bhai Jawahar Singh Ji (1867-1939) and Bhai Ram Singh Ji (1881-1933) were also perfect Gursikhs and reputed gentlemen like their ancestors, and were founders of Sri Guru Singh Sabha Faruka. The elder Mama, Bhai Bhagwan Singh Ji, remained the Jathedar of Singh Sabha and President of the Managing Committee of Khalsa High School Faruka throughout his life. Then he went to Lahore and started business and progressed a lot in the economic aspect.

Notes
- Corrected likely OCR word: "ਸਿਕਾ-ਸੱਧਰਾਂ" -> "Sik-Saddran" (Longings/Prayers).
- Corrected likely OCR word: "ਗੰਢ" -> "Gand" (Last name/Clan).
- Corrected likely OCR word: "ਮਰੱਬੇ" -> "Murabba" (Unit of land measurement, approx 25 acres per square usually, text says 25 acres/square implies big land). Note: 1 Murabba is usually 25 acres. 29 Murabba = 725 acres matches text math.

ਸਿੰਘ ਜੀ (1844-1947) ਆਪਣੇ ਮਾਪਿਆਂ ਦੇ ਘਰ ਇਕਲੈਤੇ ਪੁੱਤਰ ਸਨ
ਪਭ ਛੋਟੀ ਸੀ ਆਪ ਦੀ ਇੰਕ ਭੈਠ ਪਿਆਰ ਬਾਈ। ਬਾਲਕ ਭਾਗ ਸਿੰਘ ਦੇ ਬਚਪਨ
ਦੇ ਸਮ ਹਾਂ ਦੇ ਪਿਤਾ ਨੂੰ ਆਪਣੇ ਕਾਰੋਬਾਰ ਦੈ ਸਬੰਧ ਵਿੱਚ ਕਈ-ਕਈ ਮਹੀਨੇ ਬਾਹਰ ਰਹਿਣਾ

ਆਈ ਸੀ। ਮਾਤਾ ਜੀ ਨਾਮ ਬਾਣੀ ਦੇ ਬੜੇ ਪ੍ਰੇਮੀ ਸਨ। ਘਰ ਦੇ ਨੌਜੋਂ ਹੀ ਭਾਈ ਜੀਤ ਸਿੰਘ
ਨ ਹਰਸਾਲ ਵਿੱਚ ਮਾਤਾ ਜੀ ਨੇ ਬਾਲਕ ਭਾਗ ਸਿੰਘ ਨੂੰ ਗੁਰਮੁਖੀ-ਗੁਰਬਾਣੀ ਦੀ ਵਿੱਦਿਆ
ਦਿਵਾਈ। ਮਾਪਿਆਂ ਦੇ ਇਕੋ-ਇੱਕ ਪੁੱਤਰ ਹੋਣ ਕਾਰਨ ਘਰ ਵਿੱਚ ਬਹੁਤ ਲਾਡਲ ਸਨ। ਪਿਤਾ
ਤੇ ਦਾਦਾ ਆਪਣੇ ਇਲਾਕੇ ਦੇ ਪ੍ਰਸਿੱ ਸੱਜਣਾਂ ਵਿੱਚੋਂ ਸਨ, ਜਿਸ ਕਰਕੇ ਭਾਗ ਸਿੰਘ ਦਾ ਮੁੱਢਲਾ
ਵਨ ਸੁੱਖਾਂ ਦਾ ਬੀਤਿਆ ਤੇ ਉਹ ਆਪਣੀ ਮਨਮਾਨੀ ਕਰਨ ਦੀ ਖੁਲ੍ਹ ਰਖਦੇ ਸਨ। ਉਨ੍ਹਾਂ ਦੀ
ਰਚੀ ਰਾਗ ਵੱਲ ਸੀ, ਗਲਾ ਰਸੀਲਾ ਸੀ ਤੇ ਗਾਣ-ਵਜਾਉਣ ਦਾ ਸ਼ੌਕ ਰੱਖਦੇ ਸਨ। ਸੌ, ਜਦ ਬਾਬਾ
ਯੋਵਨ ਸਿੰਘ ਜੀ ਆਪਣੇ ਕਾਰੋਬਾਰ ਲਈ ਜਾਂਦੇ ਤਾਂ ਭਾਗ ਸਿੰਘ ਪਿੰਡ ਦੇ ਗਵੱਈਆਂ ਦੀ ਸੰਗਤ
ਵਿੱਚ ਦਿਨ ਬਤੀਤ ਕਰਦੇ।
ਇਨ੍ਹਾਂ ਦੇ ਘਰ ਦੇ ਪਿਛਲੇ ਪਾਸੇ ਇੱਕ ਮੁਸਲਮਾਨ ਫ਼ਕੀਰ ਦੀ ਮਜ਼ਾਰ ਸੀ, ਜੋ ਮਹਾਬਸ਼ਾਹ ਦੇ
ਨਾਮ ਨਾਲ ਮਸ਼ਹੂਰ ਸੀ। ਇੱਥੇ ਹਰ ਸਾਲ ਭਾਰੀ ਮੇਲਾ ਲੱਗਦਾ ਸੀ ਤੇ ਦੂਰ-ਦੂਰ ਤ ਮੁਸਲਮਾਨ
ਜਿਸਦਾ ਗਾਣਾ-ਵਜਾਣਾ ਇਲਾਕੇ ਨੇ ਬਹੁਤ ਪਸੰਦ ਕੀਤਾ ਤੇ ਇਸਨੂੰ ਇੱਥੇ ਹੀ ਰੱਖ ਲਿਆ ਗਿਆ।
ਰਾਗ ਸਿੰਘ ਜੀ ਇਸਦੀ ਸੰਗਤ ਵਿੱਚ ਰਹਿਣ ਲੱਗੇ। ਸਾਰਾ-ਸਾਰਾ ਦਿਨ ਉਸ ਮਿਰਾਸੀ ਪਾਸੋਂ ਪੱਕੇ ਰਾਗ
ਦੀਆਂ ਰੀਤਾਂ ਸਿੱਖਣੀਆਂ ਤੇ ਨਾਲ ਹੀ ਸਾਰੰਗੀ ਤੇ ਫਿਰ ਸਿਤਾਰ ਵਜਾਣੀ ਸਿੱਖੀ। ਕੁਝ ਚਿਰ ਵਿੱਚ
ਰਾਗ ਦੀ ਮਾਹਿਰੀ ਹਾਸਲ ਕੀਤੀ। ਬਾਬਾ ਜੀਵਨ ਸਿੰਘ ਨੇ ਬਥੇਰਾ ਜ਼ੋਰ ਲਾਇਆ ਕਿ ਭਾਗ ਸਿੰਘ
ਜੀ ਆਪਣੇ ਕਾਰੋਬਾਰ ਵਿੱਚ ਦਿਲਚਸਪੀ ਲੈਣ, ਪਰ ਉਨ੍ਹਾਂ ਨੇ ਪਿਤਾ ਦਾ ਕਿੱਤਾ ਦੁਕਾਨਦਾਰੀ ਨਾ
ਅਪਨਾਇਆ। ਆਪਣੇ ਗਾਣ-ਵਜਾਣ ਵਿੱਚ ਹੀ ਮਸਤ ਰਹਿੰਦੇ । ਅੰਤ ਬਾਬਾ ਜੀਵਨ ਸਿੰਘ ਜੀ ਨੇ
ਉਨ੍ਹਾਂ ਨੂੰ ਪ੍ਰੇਰਨਾ ਕੀਤੀ ਕਿ ਅਗਰ ਗਾਣਾ-ਵਜਾਣਾ ਹੀ ਕਰਨਾ ਹੈ ਤਾਂ ਗੁਰੂ ਮਹਾਰਾਜ ਦੀ ਬਾਣੀ
ਜੋ ਕਿ ਸਾਰੀ ਰਾਗਾਂ ਵਿੱਚ ਹੈ, ਉਸੇ ਨੂੰ ਹੀ ਗਾਇਨ ਕਰੋ ਤੇ ਗੁਰਬਾਣੀ ਦਾ ਕੀਰਤਨ ਕੀਤਾ ਕਰੋਂ।
ਜੀਤ ਸਿੰਘ ਜੀ ਦੀ ਧਰਮਸਾਲ ਜੋ ਘਰ ਦੇ ਨੇੜੇ ਉਸੇ ਗਲੀ ਵਿੱਚ ਹੀ ਸੀ, ਵਿੱਚ ਆਸਾ ਦੀ
ਨੇ ਤਾਉਸ ਵਜਾਣਾ ਆਰੰਭ ਕੀਤਾ ਤੇ ਫਿਰ ਸਾਰੀ ਉਮਰ ਇਸੇ ਸਾਜ਼ ਦੀ ਵਰਤੋਂ ਕੀਤੀ। ਇਉਂ
ਆਪ ਨੰ ਆਪਣੀ ਕਲਾ-ਕੋਸ਼ਲ ਨੂੰ ਗੁਰਬਾਣੀ ਦੇ ਕੀਰਤਨ ਵਿੱਚ ਢਾਲ ਕੇ ਆਪਣੀ ਲੰਮੀ ਉਮਰ
ਪੰਥ ਦੀ ਸੇਵਾ ਵਿੱਚ ਬਤੀਤ ਕੀਤੀ।
ਵਿਆਹ ਤੇ ਸੰਤਾਨ : ਭਾਈ ਭਾਗ ਸਿੰਘ ਜੀ ਦਾ ਵਿਆਹ ਸੰਨ 1860 ਦੇ ਕਰੀਬ, ਭਾਈ

ਅਮੰੱਲਕਾ ਗੰਨਾ		 English (Meaning Translation)

**Bhai Bhag Singh Ji** (1844-1947) was the only son of his parents.
Younger to him was his sister **Piar Bai**. During the childhood of child Bhag Singh, his father had to stay away for many months in connection with his business, due to which the upbringing of his childhood days largely came under the share of his mother. Mata Ji was a great lover of Naam Bani. In the Dharamsala of Bhai Jeet Singh Ji, Mata Ji got child Bhag Singh educated in Gurmukhi-Gurbani. Being the only son of parents, he was very pampered in the house. Father and grandfather were among the famous gentlemen of their area, due to which the early life of Bhag Singh was spent in comfort and he had the liberty to do as he pleased. His inclination was towards Raag (music), his throat was melodious and he was fond of singing and playing music. So, when Baba Jiwan Singh Ji went for his business, Bhag Singh used to spend the day in the company of the village singers.

Behind their house was a shrine (Mazar) of a Muslim Fakir, which was famous by the name of **Mahabshah**. Every year a big fair used to be held here and Muslims from far and wide [used to come]. [One musician name lost]... whose singing and playing was much liked by the area and he was kept here only.
Bhag Singh Ji started living in his company. Spending whole days learning proper Raag tunes from that Mirasi and also learned to play Sarangi and then Sitar. In some time, he acquired mastery in Raag. Baba Jiwan Singh tried hard that Bhag Singh Ji should take interest in his business, but he did not adopt the father's profession of shopkeeping. He remained engrossed in his singing and playing. Finally Baba Jiwan Singh Ji persuaded him that if you have to do singing and playing, then sing only the Baani of Guru Maharaj which is all in Raags, and perform Kirtan of Gurbani.

In the Dharamsala of [Bhai] Jeet Singh Ji which was near the house in the same street, [he started performing] Asa Ki Var... He started playing **Taus** and then used this instrument all his life. Thus, molding his art and skill into the Kirtan of Gurbani, he spent his long life in the service of the Panth.

**Marriage and Progeny:**
Bhai Bhag Singh Ji was married around the year 1860 at a young age to **Sat Bharai Ji**, the elder daughter of Bhai Bhag Singh Ji Gand of Faruka. For a long time, no child was born in their house and the first child **Sri Sant Bhai Ram Kishan Ji**...

Notes
- Corrected likely OCR word: "ਪਭ" -> "Bhain" (Sister).
- Corrected likely OCR word: "ਇਕਲੈਤੇ" -> "Eklota" (Only son).

ਦੇਣ ੯੪੫ =੨		 English (Meaning Translation)

**(1792-1888)**: [He was born] in 1879 with the blessings and prayer of the Mahant Sahib of the Shahpur Dera of the Seva Panthi sect. Regarding the birth of this child... it is written in 'Sant Gatha' of [Bhai] Vir Singh Ji...

One [day] Bhai Ram Kishan Ji, while touring with his Mandli (group), arrived at village Faruka, district Shahpur (now Sargodha). Next morning, the Kirtan of Asa Di Var was to be performed. Udasi Baba Karam Das, who knew Bhai Bhag Singh Ji Ragi of Faruka, was also there. He [asked] Bhai Bhag Singh Ji to perform Kirtan...

When [Adi Granth] was being closed... Bhai Bhag Singh Ji sat there with his head down. Baba Karam Das Ji asked from nearby why he was sitting. He said, "Maharaj Ji, it has been about 18 years since his marriage, but still no child has been born. Please be kind and give some infallible word so that his lineage may continue with the world."

Hearing this, **Sant Bhai Ram Kishan Ji** said in a color (mood) of ecstasy: "Doesn't he perform Kirtan of the Guru? The root of the Guru's Kirtaniya (singer) is always green. The Guru will fulfill your wish. A diamond (**Hira**) will be born in your house. Say 'Dhan Guru Nanak', 'Dhan Guru Nanak' and stay happy."
Then he said to Bhai Bhag Singh Ji's wife to recite Sukhmani Sahib daily. Saying this, he asked for a bowl of water... washed his feet's toe in the water... and ordered to drink the water.

It is the statement of Bhai Bhag Singh Ji that after 11 months of this boon of Bhai Ram Kishan Ji, Waheguru blessed a son in their house. Taking the son, they appeared at the Dera of Sant Bhai Ram Kishan Ji at Shahpur. The ceremony of Chola (initiation dress) and Naming was done here. Bhai Ram Kishan Ji named this boy **'Hira Singh'** with his own holy tongue.
This very boy grew up to become **Bhai Hira Singh Ji**, the 'Amolak Hira' (Precious Diamond) of Khalsa Panth and a devoted Sikh of the Guru's house, true to his word and brave in deeds... unsurpassed Kirtaniya that with his Kirtan power he brought staunchest atheists to the Guru's shelter, created love for Sikhism in the hearts of many Arya Samajis, made Muslims say 'Dhan Guru Nanak' and swayed gatherings of 25-30 thousand people in divine color.

After Bhai Hira Singh Ji, two more sons were born in the house of Bhai Bhag Singh Ji - **Bhai Gurmukh Singh Ji** (1882-1957) and **Bhai Pradhan Singh Ji** (1895-1959).
Mata Sat Bharai Ji was of a very cool temperament and lover of Naam Bani... She used to serve food and water to visitors in the Dharamsala with great love and devotion...

Notes
- Corrected likely OCR word: "ਰਾਹ ਹੋਵਾ ਧੰਥੀ" -> "Seva Panthi" (Sect).
- Corrected likely OCR word: "ਪੰਡ" -> "Pind" (Village).

/ ਨ % 9 ਕ2 ,&. ਨ? 4 ਤੱ		 English (Meaning Translation)

(Khalsa Samachar, 29-10-19[19?]).

**Participation in Panthic Service**: Soon after the birth of Bhai Hira Singh Ji, **Bhai Bhag Singh Ji** started his Kirtan tours in the area of **Pothohar**. In those days [Sants?] were preaching a lot in the areas. Bhai Bhag Singh Ji contributed according to his capacity.

In the year **1897**, Bhai Bhag Singh Ji started performing Kirtan joining with his son **Bhai Hira Singh Ji**, and then for 25-26 years, reaching countries within the nation and abroad, they sounded the drum of Guru Nanak's Name and connected countless souls to the Guru's feet.

Their sweet melodious throat, high vibrating tune and the Gurbani sung in simple tunes of proper Raag used to bring a wave in the congregations. When in the solitude of Amrit Vela (early morning), **Bapu Ji** (Bhai Bhag Singh Ji was often remembered by the name 'Bapu Ji') used to move the bow on the **Taus** and sing the alap in a sweet voice, then the hearts of the listeners used to get pulled.

Bhai Bhag Singh Ji was a master of Raag. There was a special distinct juice (Ras) in his throat; he was very firm in rhythm and beat (Sur-Taal) and used to get engrossed in Kirtan while performing.
According to the late **Master Karam Singh Ji**, Assistant Secretary Chief Khalsa Diwan, his father was instrumental in filling the power of Kirtan in the consciousness of Bhai Hira Singh Ji, and with the blessing of Kirtan, taking Bhai Hira Singh Ji to heights...

Once at Sri Akal Takht, [a competition?] between some famous Ragis and Bhai Bhag Singh Ji... [The condition was] to sing in the same Raag as written in Sri Guru Granth Sahib. Many... were sung, but in the end Bhai Bhag Singh [succeeded] in this...

In August 1916... a poem in Khalsa Samachar dated 10...

Notes
- Corrected likely OCR word: "ਪੋਨੋਹਾਰ" -> "Pothohar" (Region in West Punjab known for Sikh population).
- Corrected likely OCR word: "ਤਾਊਜ" -> "Taus" (Peacock shaped string instrument).

/4ਛਕੜ` - 2੭
ਵਿੱਚ ਸੁਲਦੇ ਪਏ ਸਨ, ਝੱਟ ਬੋਲ ਪਏ, 'ਪਹਿਲਾਂ ਤਾਂ
੩		 English (Meaning Translation)

...Asa Di Var [sung by them]... we obtained much benefit.

In the year 1926, Bhai Bhag Singh Ji suffered a heavy shock of the passing away of his beloved son **Bhai Hira Singh Ji**, but he accepted the Will of the Satguru and kept reciting Baani. For two-three years, he remained occupied in calming his mind while staying at a solitary place in his village Faruka.

In the year 1928, Bhai Bhag Singh Ji (at the age of 84 years) went to see **Sriman Bhai Sahib Bhai Vir Singh Ji** along with his younger [son]. Bhai Sahib ordered Bapu Ji: "Instead of Bhai Hira Singh Ji, form a Jatha with **Bhai Pradhan Singh** (youngest son) and engage in Panthic service." Bhai Bhag Singh Ji obeyed his order and forming a Jatha afresh, performed the service of Kirtan for about 6-7 years. On original Guru Nanak Dev Ji's birthday, in the Pandal of Chief Khalsa Diwan at Nankana Sahib...

**Nature and Character:**
Bhai Bhag Singh Ji's life was very simple, pure and clean. He did not hesitate to speak straight and true. Food was very simple and little - eating two rotis (bread) with one vegetable or dal. His health remained fine till the last breath. Up to the age of 95 years, he used to walk four-five miles easily. The vision of eyes remained intact till the end and he could read the Path of Sri Guru Granth Sahib and Gurmukhi newspaper easily without spectacles all his life.

Since he himself was firm in rhythm and beat (Sur-Taal), therefore he could not tolerate out-of-tune singing or out-of-beat sound. Whenever someone in the Jatha made such a mistake, he used to look with a stern eye.

There was ample element of humor in Bapu Ji. He used to [diffuse] a serious situation in a light manner. At the age of hundred years, it is a difficult task to consider life as life, but Bapu Ji used to smile in his last days just as in youth. The courage to live was present in him like young men. once I said, "Bapu Ji, if you cross one more year you will be fully hundred years old!" He replied with readiness, "So am I dying anytime soon?"
Once some women were talking, "Upon Bapu Ji's death we will make sweet rice and distribution (Parshad) etc." He was sleeping in the upper room (Chubara), he immediately spoke up, "First [let me die]..."

Notes
- Corrected likely OCR word: "ਪੁ" -> "Putar" (Son) - context of "younger son" implied.
- Corrected likely OCR word: "ਕੌੜੀ" -> "Kaudi/Kauri" (Bitter/Stern) eye.
- Corrected likely OCR word: "ਲਹਿਜੇ" -> "Lehje" (Tone/Manner).

ਤਮ ਵਰੇ ਤੇ ਗੁਰਪੁਰੀ ਪਿਆਨਾ ! ਸੰਨ 1936-37 ਵਿੱਚ, ਜਦ ਬਾਪੂ ਜੀ ਤਕਰੀਬਨ 93
ਜਰ ਰਨ ਦੇ ਦਿਆਂ ਤੇ ਜਾਣਾ ਬੰਦ ਕਰ ਦਿਤਾ ਸੀ।ਪਰ ੬

ਵੀ ਸਤਿਗੁਰੁ ਨੇ ਬਖ਼ਸ਼ਿਆ ਹੋਇਆ ਸੀ, ਆਪਣੀ ਨਿੱਜ ਕ੍ਰਿਆ, ਇਸ਼ਨਾਨ ਆਦਿਕ ਅਜ਼ੀਰਲੇ

ਰਿ		 English (Meaning Translation)

[...He used to follow the maxim that] 'When you live by being detached [you can keep others happy]. [If you yourself] get fed up with life, then by doing so you cannot keep others happy.' He used to remain happy himself and [gave happiness] to others.

**Last Time and Departure for Guru's Abode:**
In the year 1936-37, when Bapu Ji was about 93 [years old], he stopped going on [long] tours. But... he continued the service of Kirtan in the Dharamsala of [his] village till quite late age. The Satguru had bestowed such physical strength that he used to do his personal chores, bathing etc. himself till the last time. Going out to the fields/jungle (for nature's call) and walking according to need [was routine].

In **February-March 1947**, he felt himself a bit unwell. At that time his second son **Bhai Gurmukh Singh Ji** Giani, who was employed as Religious and Punjabi teacher at Chiefs College Lahore, took him from Faruka to Lahore for service and treatment.
And here on **23 April 1947**, after living an age of about **103 years**, he departed for the Guru's Abode.

- Corrected likely OCR word: "ਸ਼ੁਸ਼" -> "Khush" (Happy).

੭੭		 English (Meaning Translation)

**Bhai Hira Singh Ji**
"Guru Nanak, You have bestowed this gift."

**Birth:** As we have already mentioned, Bhai Hira Singh Ji was born in the year **1879** at the house of Bhai Bhag Singh Ji with the blessings and prayer of Sant Bhai Ram Kishan Ji of Shahpur Dera. At the time when this beautiful child was born, a wave of happiness ran through the whole family and congratulations started coming from all sides. But [the greatest] happiness was to **Baba Jiwan Singh Ji** who had seen the face of a [grand]child in the house after full 35 years.

**Education:** He received primary education of Gurmukhi Gurbani in the Dharamsala of **Bhai Mahna Singh Ji**... But after a short while due to domestic hurdles the studies had to be stopped and worldly...
Gurmukh beloved **Bhai Ishar Singh Ji Khurana** used to tell that he was also a student of Bhai Mahna Singh Ji at that time. According to him - "Bhai Hira Singh Ji was very fond of reading Gurbani and Gur-History and he used to remain ahead of other students. Even in childhood his inclination was towards reading religious books.
Apart from acquiring the understanding of meanings of Guru Granth Sahib Ji, he also studied Granths like **Suraj Prakash**, **Gur Bilas** and **Varan Bhai Gurdas** etc.
He memorized a lot of Gurbani and in this task he kept getting encouragement and inspiration from the practical life of his grandfather **Baba Jiwan Singh Ji**.

In the year 1926, when this author used to recite the daily Nitnem and Paath of Baani to Bhai Sahib during his illness, one day he told me that, "At your age, apart from the Baanis of Nitnem, I had [memorized] Sukhmani Sahib and Bavan... [Akhri]..."

Notes
- Corrected likely OCR word: "ਪਨਮ" -> "Janam" (Birth).
- Corrected likely OCR word: "ਸਗੀਰ" -> "Sharir" (Body/Health).

ਅੰਓਲਾ` ਲਾੀਫਨ` - 2?		 English (Meaning Translation)

He stayed for about one and a half years in the feet of Saints [Sant Attar Singh Ji?]. He went to Sindh with the Sant Ji...
After spending some months in the company of the Saint... and used to be engrossed in Simran... Bhai Hira Singh Ji also used to participate in Bhajan...

Then when the Jatha of Saints [returned]... appeared in the Dera... and requested that Bhai Hira Singh is a "Hira" (Diamond), give blessing that staying at his own home he may recite Naam and make others recite. ...Saints gave blessings to Bhai Hira Singh along with Bapu Ji and sent them off.

**Return to Faruka:**
When he reached his village Faruka, the residents of the town were very pleased to see his saintly attire and saintly nature. A white cotton tunic (Gatra) on the body, Kachhera up to knees, a round white turban on head and Gatra-Kirpan in neck, an iron Gadva (pot) in one hand and Simrana (rosary) in the other - all these were very impressive.
When... people gathered and said, "The [son] of Bhai Bhag Singh... amazes everyone." Mast eyes and radiant [face]...
Bhai Sahib's mother Sat Bharai used to say... "Whatever words come out of the mouth of this 'Sadhu', they come true." ...
Mata Ji used to say... "Attire and signs are like saints... If he stays in this field (household)..."

**Departure for Sri Amritsar:**
Finally, how long could this son of a Saint stay in his home? The atmosphere he had left behind in the company of Sant Attar Singh Ji, where could he find it [here]? Dispassion kept arising in the inner self and mind did not settle in Faruka. The passion for Satsang kept getting stronger in the heart. Convincing his wife to get ready to go to **Sri Amritsar**, one day he asked for permission from his parents. Father tried hard, Mother pleaded a lot...

Notes
- Corrected likely OCR word: "ਡੇਢ" -> "One and a half" (years).
- Corrected likely OCR word: "ਸਿੰਧ" -> "Sindh" (Province).

...relatives [also] put many hurdles to stop him, but one who is colored in His love, who can stop his way?
[He] departed. Before leaving, the wife wanted to check what will [we eat/do] there... "We are going to the city of Guru Ram Das, He himself will do everything."

**At Amritsar:**
Reaching Sri Amritsar, the couple first arrived at **Kucha Basti Ram**. (Here lived **Bhai Amir Singh Ji**, guru-brother of Bhai Jiwan Singh Ji of Faruka, whose Dharamsala in Faruka was in the street of Bhai Hira Singh and which has been mentioned in 'Birth Place' section.) Bhai Ji welcomed the couple and gave accommodation with great love, but after a short while, he took a room on rent in the same street and moved there.
From here, giving broom service in the circumambulation (Parikarma) of Sri Darbar Sahib morning and evening, doing service of the Sarovar (holy tank), serving water at Chhabils and cleaning shoes (Joda), this was the daily program.

**Service of Khalsa Tract Society:**
This was the time when Guru-beloved **Bhai Sahib (Bhai Vir Singh)** used to do service... The attire was such that no one could recognize him. This mention is of the year **1896** when the age of Bhai Sahib Bhai Vir Singh Ji was 24 years and that of Bhai Hira Singh was 17 years. The residence of Bhai Sahib Bhai Vir Singh was then in Katra Garba Singh. By the Creator's will, how the sight of Bhai Sahib Ji fell on young Bhai Hira Singh. There was one way to reach Sri Darbar Sahib and Bhai Hira Singh Ji also used to do Sevain Parikarma at Amrit Vela. So his discerning eye recognized that this young man is capable of doing service with dedication. Therefore, he engaged Bhai Hira Singh in a service of **Khalsa Tract Society**. Due to this, he not only got the opportunity to read the tracts of Sriman Bhai Sahib Ji, but also obtained the clue of Bhai Sahib being [a great soul].

Along with the service of Tract Society, his routine of service at Sri Darbar Sahib continued as before. In this regard, **Sir Manmohan Singh Ji**, 'Kails' Wale... writes in 'Khalsa Samachar': "We see this young man (Bhai Hira Singh) in the morning at Amrit Vela... at Darbar Sahib... waking up early in the morning... works whole day... it is surprising. Bhai Sahib Ji caught the arm of this young man working in the afternoon..."

- Corrected likely OCR word: "ਪੁੰਜ" -> "Pujj" (Reach/Arrive).
- Corrected likely OCR word: "ਕੌਲੇ" -> "Joda" (Shoes/Sandals - doing shoe service). Or could be "Kole" (Bowls), but context of Seva usually implies Jora/Shoes.

...[Bhai Sahib was so happy] that he appointed him a 'Computitor' in Khalsa Tract Society. Bhai Hira Singh Ji [started working]... 1896...
Some gentlemen have written that [this happened in]... 1898... But our information is that (pages 63)...

They had brought very little goods, utensils and clothes from home. The winter season arrived. The wife saved some money from small earnings and bought a blanket. And when he used to go to Sri Darbar Sahib early morning, she would make him wear this blanket.
[One day] he took off his blanket and made some [needy] gentleman wear it. When he came home, on wife's asking, he said, "His need was greater than mine." Many such incidents...

...practiced Kirtan more.
After some time, Bapu Ji [Bhai Bhag Singh]... also came. Then getting relieved from the service of Society, with the advice and blessing of Sriman Bhai Sahib (Vir Singh) Ji, and taking the support of Satguru, he [formed a Jatha] with his father...

ਇੱਕ ਮੀ		 English (Meaning Translation)

...started. This time was the end of year **1897**.
In those days, **Giani Thakur Singh Ji** usually used to be with the Jatha of Bhai Bhag Singh Hira Singh Ji.
Where there is **Guru Ka Bagh** (Amritsar) now, there used to be an old-style [garden/park]. Here [they] had attached a [stage?] in front of which fountains used to flow. Daily evening, one satsang...

He had already studied... and Gur-History, and [whatever was lacking] he obtained from the company of **Sant Attar Singh Ji**. And the knowledge of Parmarth (spirituality) increased further in the Satsang of **Bhai Sahib Bhai Vir Singh Ji**. Life was molded in the service of Sri Darbar Sahib and the Master had blessed him with a melodious throat.
Due to these qualities, a strange charm used to bind in his Kirtan and the attendance of Sangat started increasing day by day. In a short time, the fame of his Kirtan [spread] in Amritsar...

**Rai Bahadur Bisakha Singh Ji** (1880-1959), famous contractor of Delhi, told in one of his articles (Sher-e-Punjab, 2 September 1951) - "In 1898 I heard his Kirtan for the first time when he was in youth stage at a wedding..."
The late **Bhai Sudh Singh Ji** told in one of his articles (Khalsa Samachar, 2-9-70) - "In 1901 when I was a student of Updeshak School Gujranwala, Bhai Bhag Singh Bhai Hira Singh Ji came there. The bloom of youth was on his Kirtan at that time... He had a nice full beautiful beard and his mood used to get emotional while performing Kirtan and Prayer... Sangat used to get lost... flying in that Mandal..."

...very sweet melodious... in his throat [was] Amrit...
'Gursikh Ashiq Sabad Re' (Gursikh is lover of the Word) - listening to [his] Kirtan, sacrificing body, mind and wealth...
In every Diwan/Samagam... magnetic pull in the Guru's Sangat...

- Corrected likely OCR word: "ਸਤਰੰਗ" -> "Satsang".
- Corrected likely OCR word: "ਅਭਿਆਘ" -> "Abhyas" (Practice/Study).

੪		 English (Meaning Translation)

**Backdrop of Singh Sabha Movement**
With the end of Sikh Raj, one [factor was that] Sikhs themselves had fallen into decline.
Attacks of non-believers and missionaries... like termite were eating [the Panth]. The number of Sikhs had fallen to such a low that where during Sikh Raj the count was near one crore, in 1881 it remained only 1,853,437.

On one side the preaching of Christian missionaries and on the other contrary practices...
In the Parikarma of Sri Darbar Sahib, idols were worshipped...
In 1873... **Pandit Shardha Ram Phillauri** (1839-1881), the author of Hindu Aarti 'Om Jai Jagdish Hare', while performing Katha in Guru Ka Bagh, spoke some words against the glory of Guru Sahibs. This was like the last straw on the camel's back. The blood of Khalsa boiled. As a result,
To discuss these issues, **Sardar Thakur Singh Sandhawalia** along with other prominent Sikhs called a meeting...
...Four Sikh students were taken to England and converted to Christianity...
After staying there for about one and a half years, re-converting them to Sikh religion...
Later in May 19XX... Maharaja [Duleep Singh?]...

A big Diwan was held, in which prominent gentlemen of the Panth participated and **Sri Guru Singh Sabha** was established. This was the beginning of Singh Sabha Lahore.
Then in 1879 Singh Sabha Lahore was formed and Singh Sabhas were established at places outside also. In 1903 a representative Jatha of Sabhas [formed] Khalsa Diwan...

Notes
- Corrected likely OCR word: "ਕੱਖ ਗਜ" -> "Sikh Raj" (Sikh Rule).
- Corrected likely OCR word: "ਉ" -> "Oh" (That/It).

ਭਾਈ ਹੀਰਾ ਸਿੰਘ ਜੀ ਨੇ ਇਸ ਸਮਾਗਮ ਦੀ ਹਾਜ਼ਰੀ ਦੀਵਾਨ ਦੇ ਮੋਢੀਆਂ ਦੇ ਨਾਲ ਹੋ ਕੇ ਭਗੇ
ਫਿਰ ਆਪ ਨੇ ਆਪਣੀ ਸੇਵਾ ਦੀਵਾਨ ਦੇ ਅਰਪਨ ਕਰਕੇ ਅਤੁੱਟ ਸੇਵਾ ਕੀਤੀ। ਇਸ ਸਬੰਧ

_ ਭਾਈ ਸਾਹਿਬ ਨੇ ਥਾਂ-ਥਾਂ ਧਾਰਮਿਕ ਦੀਵਾਨਾਂ ਵਿੱਚ ਪੁੱਜ ਕੇ ਸਿੱਖਾਂ ਨੂੰ ਧਾਰਮਕ ਤੌਰ ਉੱਤੇ
ਆ ਤਾ, ਅੰਮ੍ਰਿਤ ਪ੍ਰਚਾਰ ਕੀਤੇ ਤੇ ਰਹਿਤ-ਬਹਿਤ ਵੱਲ ਸਿੱਖ ਨੌਜੁਆਨਾਂ ਨੰ ਪ੍ਰੇਰਿਆ, ਗੁਰ
ਅਨੁਕੂਲ ਕਰਨ ਲਈ ਤਾਣ ਵੱਸ ਰਹੁ-ਰੀਤੀ ਗੁਰਮਤਿ ਤੇ ਸਿੱਖ ਰਵਾਇਤ
ਹਰਿਦੁਆਰ ਲਿਜਾਣੇ ਜਿ ਇਆ ਸ਼ਰਾਧ, ਨ੍ਰਾਤੇ ਵਰਤ, ਵੇਦੀ ਨਾਲ ਵਿਆਹ, ਰਲ
ਅਰਕ ਲੋ ----------.੨ ਗ੩ਆਂ ਤੂ ਗੁਰਮੀਤ ਵ੍ਰਿੱਧ ਦਰਸ		 English (Meaning Translation)

At that time the Singh Sabha movement was in full force and Bhai Sahib reached various places in religious Diwans and made efforts for the fulfillment of Panthic objectives. Many reports of Gurmat preaching regarding [Singh Sabha] efforts and Anand Karaj ceremonies conducted by him are found published in Panthic newspapers of that time. In many functions, Giani Thakur Singh Ji used to be with him.

Being a preacher, the mention of Bhai Hira Singh Ji's association with famous Panth-Sevaks of that time is noteworthy. With **Bhai Sahib Bhai Vir Singh Ji**, he had a relationship of Satsang, and along with him, Bhai Hira Singh Ji had the honor of serving the Panth together with **Sardar Sundar Singh Ji Majithia**, **Sardar Harbans Singh Attari**, and **Sardar Trilochan Singh Ji**.
Due to the passing away of **Professor Gurmukh Singh** of Oriental College Lahore, the prominent worker of Singh Sabha, in 1898 and **Giani Ditt Singh Ji** in 1901, the work of Khalsa Diwan Lahore slowed down. Therefore in 1902, a representative body of the Panth, **Chief Khalsa Diwan** was formed and its President **Bhai Sahib Bhai Arjan Singh Ji Bagrian** and Secretary **Sardar Sundar Singh Ji Majithia** were elected. The first congregation of this Diwan was held on 30 October 1902 at Malwai Bunga, Sri Darbar Sahib.
Bhai Hira Singh Ji participated in this congregation along with the founders of the Diwan. Then dedicating his services to the Diwan, he performed ceaseless service. In this regard, some words from the main article of **'Khalsa Samachar'** dated 9 September 1926 [are quoted]:

"Bhai Hira Singh Ji Ragi appeared in the field in the capacity of a General of the Sikh Panth, and just as by the order of Sher-e-Punjab Ranjit Singh, Sardar Hari Singh Nalwa... established the coin of bravery of Sikhs up to the walls of Kabul and Kandahar... and enhanced the glory of Khalsa, similarly Bhai Hira Singh Ji Ragi, preaching under the order of Chief Khalsa Diwan, in small towns of Punjab, Kashmir, Frontier Province, U.P., Sindh, Bengal, Assam and Burma, sounded such a lion's roar (Singh-Naad) of Sikhism that every door and wall echoed with the resonance of **'Satnam Sri Waheguru'**... added four moons (glory) to Sikhism..."

Bhai Sahib reached religious Diwans at various places and [made Sikhs firm] on religion, conducted Amrit Prachar and inspired Sikh youth towards Rehat-Behat (Sikh code of conduct). To make the life according to Gurmat... he stressed on abandoning rituals like carrying bones to Haridwar, Shradhs, Navratras, fasting, wedding by Bedi etc.

Notes

- Corrected likely OCR word: "ਦਿਗ ਵਿਜੇ" -> "Dig Vijay" (World Conquest/Grand Victory).

...The cleverness of Brahmins had alienated the rich Sikhs of **Chakkri** from the Singh Sabhias.
...No one even offered water to Bhai Sahib. He spent the night at a serai nearby.

[Next day, in the Diwan]... **Sardar Jagat Singh Sawhney** of Chakkri also arrived. He was a prominent leader of the area. When Bhai Sahib challenged the self-respect of Sikhs regarding the insult of Singh Sabha, their religious pride woke up, and there was a stir among the Sikhs.
Whispers started among the sitting Sikhs. The Sangat regained its non-secular pride from Bhai Sahib's words, but Sardar Jagat Singh of Chakkri was totally won over by Bhai Sahib's words. He got up and expressed his desire to take Amrit and took a pledge to organize Amrit Prachar in his village Chakkri. (This account is based on an article by **Bhai Teja Singh M.A.** published in 'Khalsa Samachar' dated 25 March 1971).

This story is just a sample of Bhai Hira Singh Ji's Singh Sabha preaching.
News of many such other incidents are found, when in difficult and tough times...
Singh Sabha Movement and Chief Khalsa Diwan...

/ ਨੀ 3੪ %ਡੂਗ ਤਕ ਤੂ _		 English (Meaning Translation)

...nor were there any good means of transport.

To fulfill the shortage of Sikh preaching from many places, appeals used to come to Chief Khalsa Diwan, on which the Diwan used to send Bhai Hira Singh Ji to such places.
In **March 1903**, on the appeal of local Sangats of **Peshawar**, efforts made for that...
**Appeal:** Beloved Panth! There is a dire need of preaching in the area of Peshawar. Especially in Peshawar (which is a center of Sikhism), Sikhism is declining day by day... sacrificing sacred hair they are entering the [Arya] Samaj. Seeing many such miseries, it has been considered that all these deficits are due to lack of preaching...

Reaching places like **Mardan**, **Garhi Kapura**, **Rustam**, **Akora** etc., [he] did Gurmat preaching for one month.
[Opponents] created a lot of noise and tried to disrupt the Diwan, but when Bhai Hira Singh Ji stood up and answered tactfully, everyone became quiet. In this side, there was much hatred spread against Singh Sabha, but with the preaching of this Jatha, people embraced it.

Similarly, in 'Khalsa Samachar' dated 24 April 1904, the following report is found under the headline **'Preaching in Kahuta'** from **Sardar Asa Singh Ji**:
In this town, for the last five days **Bhai Bhag Singh Ji, Bhai Hira Singh Ji** have come, who through their captivating Kirtan have waxed the stone hearts of the Sangat to such an extent that... who was that heart which listening to...
Listening to the love-filled Kirtan... dispassion [arose]...

Notes
- Corrected likely OCR word: "ਮੋਮ" -> "Mom" (Wax/Melt).
- Corrected likely OCR word: "ਬੁਤ" -> "Bahut" (Much).

___ ਇੱਥੇ ਇਹ ਦੱਸਣਾ ਕੁਥਾਏ ਨਹੀਂ ਹੋਵੇਗਾ ਕਿ ਸਿੰਘ ਸਭਾ ਲਹਿਰ ਦੇ ਬਾਨੀ ਤੇ ਚੀਫ਼ ਖ਼ਾਲਸਾ		 English (Meaning Translation)

...Apart from the annual sessions of Chief Khalsa Diwan, Diwans used to be held on occasions of Diwali and Vaisakhi. Sample reports of Diwans held in 1904...
"On the occasion of Diwali, Diwans were held on 5, 6, 7 November. [In the morning]... Ragis Bhai Partap Singh, Hira Singh performed Gurbani Kirtan... whole Sangat was extremely pleased..."
"...Asa Di Var was performed... Bhai Bhag Singh Hira Singh...
When Bhai Hira Singh Ji used to read 'Sir Ditiyan Je Mile Khasam' (If by giving head the Master is met) or 'Ram Simar Ram Simar Ihe Tero Kaj Hai' (Remember Ram, Remember Ram, this is your only work) in a very lovely tune, then everyone's mind used to get pulled..."
-- Servant of Panth, **Sundar Singh Majithia**

Dedicating his service for the funds of Chief Khalsa Diwan, expecting all the money received in that time to be surrendered to the Diwan, he also used to collect more money according to capacity and sent it, and kept making strong appeals to Sangats even in newspapers.
As a sample, one appeal which was published in 'Khalsa Samachar' of **29-4-1908** is as follows:

**"Will you also accomplish some task?"**
"Beloved Khalsa Ji! Daily new means are revealed for Panthic progress and it is said that now Chief Khalsa Diwan should do this, now do that... But you also know that for every work the first requirement is of Maya (money).
For Maya, that fortunate time will be brought by Satguru only when Sangats will bring heaps of money as Daswandh every year and surrender to Guru Panth. However, now the proposal of small effort of 'Chawani Fund' (Four Anna Fund) is before you for about three years, if you make it happen instead of just 'saying', then the boat will sail across.
What is the reason that even this small task has not reached full success? It was required that by today this task should have been remembered by every child, poor and rich in Sikhs..."

The purpose of describing the above sample incidents is to show how much attraction was there in Bhai Hira Singh Ji's heart for the progress of Chief Khalsa Diwan and how much yearning was in his heart for Sikh preaching, the banner of which was lifted by the founders of the Diwan in those days.

It would not be out of place to mention here that the founders of Singh Sabha movement and Chief Khalsa Diwan...

- Corrected likely OCR word: "ਸਿਰ ਦਿੱਤਆ" -> "Sir Ditiyan" (By giving head).
- Corrected likely OCR word: "ਚੁਆਨੀ" -> "Chawani" (Four Annas - a quarter rupee).

ਬਣਾਏ ਪ੍ਰੋਗਰਾਮ ਕਿਉਂ ਨਾ ਕਾਮਯਾਬ ਹੁੰਦੇ ? - ਤੂੰ
ਉਪ੍ਰੋਕਤ ਮਿਸਾਲ ਤਾਂ ਮੁਖੀ ਸੇਵਕਾਂ ਦੀ ਹੈ ਜੋ ਕਿ ਦੀਵਾਨ ਦੇ ਪ੍ਰੋਗਰਾਮ ਉਲੀਕਦੇ ਨ
ਪਾਲਿਸੀ ਬਣਾਂਦੇ ਸਨ। ਪਰ ਇਨ੍ਹਾਂ ਪ੍ਰੋਗਰਾਮਾਂ ਨੂੰ ਅਮਲੀ ਜਾਮਾ ਪਹਿਨਾਣ ਵਾਲੈ
ਦੇ ਪ੍ਰਚਾਰਕ ਸਨ, ਉਹ ਵੀ ਉੱਚੇ ਜੀਵਨ ਤੇ ਲਗਨ ਵਾਲੇ ਸੱਜਣ ਸਨ, ਕਿਉਂਜਿ 'ਭ ?

36 - ਅਸ਼ਲਕਾ ਹੰਠਾ ਰ੍		 English (Meaning Translation)

...The main servants of the Diwan were themselves of high character and ideal Gursikhs.
...[Within them] was the passion for selfless service and pure Gurmat preaching.
**Sriman Bhai Sahib Bhai Vir Singh Ji** was a great high, saintly personality who can be called the [Soul?] of the Diwan, but his companions were also owners of high [character?]. For example, everyone knows the high conduct of **Sardar Sundar Singh Ji Majithia**. But I want to tell here an incident seen with my own eyes which influenced me greatly. This matter is of year **1920-21**, when I was studying in [4th?] class. At that time Bhai Hira Singh Ji's residence was at **Chowk Karori** Amritsar. It was often the effort of Sardar Sundar Singh Ji that whenever Bhai Hira Singh Ji stayed in Amritsar for two-four days upon returning from preaching tours, he should perform Kirtan of Asa Di Var at **Majitha House** occasionally.

Accordingly, on one such occasion, Bhai Sahib took me along too at Amrit Vela. Bapu Ji and Jatha had gone to sleep at Majitha House at night itself. At about 4 AM, Bhai Sahib and I reached Majitha House walking. Ahead Bapu Ji and Jatha were performing Kirtan.
It was the days of Assu-Katak (autumn), there was mild cold. In the room where Kirtan was happening, there was dim light like a zero-watt bulb gives. One person... whether anyone else has entered or not. Two-and-a-half hours continuous pure Kirtan.
...Sitting steadfast in cross-legged posture (Chaukra). He had covered his face with a sheet. **Rani Sahib** and other ladies were sitting in the adjacent room. Bhai Sahib bowed before Maharaj and sat near his Vaja (harmonium) and I sat behind him...
...remained happening, but the gentleman sitting wrapped up remained sitting in absolute stillness. I kept watching with attention. Neither he changed his sitting posture, nor lifted his knee, nor looked towards Ragi Singhs. And I kept wondering that some Saint-Mahatma has come, but where is Sardar Ji himself?
...[Later I found] that was [Sardar Sundar] Singh Ji, who was so connected and sitting absolutely engrossed. And about **Sardar Tarlochan Singh Ji** it is also said that in his youth... he used to fill the presence at Sri Darbar Sahib... and used to do service in Parikarma.
Such were the lives of the [pillars] of Singh Sabha and Chief Khalsa Diwan. Then why wouldn't the tasks initiated by such colored leaders be accomplished? Why wouldn't the programs made [by them] succeed?

The above example is of the chief servants who used to chalk out the programs and make policies of the Diwan. But those who were to practicalize these programs... the preachers... they were also gentlemen of high life and dedication, because if the preacher's own life is not high, his lectures [will have no effect]...

Notes
- Corrected likely OCR word: "ਨੈਂਦਾ" -> "Sunda" (Sundar Singh).
- Corrected likely OCR word: "ਪਰਚਾਰਕ" -> "Pracharak" (Preacher).

% % ਜੋ ੧ %		 English (Meaning Translation)

Know that [the reasons/evils] for the fulfillment of whose objectives our elders did hard labor...
To remove the [ill-practices] Singh Sabha servants made such efforts...
Those have again entered among us today...
...rituals are performed according to [Gurmariada? or opposite?]. Leaving aside administering Amrit to boys and girls, sometimes it is not even mentioned. Garlands/Sehras around neck in presence of Guru Maharaj, photographers hopping here and there and many other kinds of... which were never even seen in those days.
Birth and death [ceremonies] are also not performed according to full Guru's tradition now. Picking bones (Phul) and taking them to Haridwar, which were declared against Gurmat, now even big honorable Sants are taken to Kiratpur etc. places which is not according to Gurmat.
Many other such evil practices have entered our society, to remove which and to revive the constructive forces, there is as much need now as there was at the time of Singh Sabha movement.

On the next few pages, an attempt has been made to give samples of the struggle done by Bhai Hira Singh Ji in this regard.

Notes
- "Phul Chun-ne" refers to collecting ashes/bones after cremation.
- "Sehra" is the wedding garland/veil tied on groom's forehead.
